**Codex pre-push round 9 (1 P0 + 1 P1).** (P0) **Dispute ↔ settlement ordering** — the statement dispute path keyed on the `payments` row (`stripe_charge_id`), which doesn't exist until `payment_intent.succeeded` settles, and Stripe doesn't guarantee ordering; a `charge.dispute.created` delivered first skipped reversal and a later succeeded settled clawed-back money. `handleDisputeCreated` now resolves the statement by `dispute.payment_intent` (not the payments row); `reverseStatementCascadeForDispute` reverses a settled cascade OR, when the dispute precedes settlement, **clears the statement's active PI** so the racing/late succeeded fails the active-PI binding and records an orphan instead of settling. (P1) **Reverted the global-total reader exclusions** — excluding payer rows from business-wide cash/revenue made paid statements vanish entirely; the exclusion now lives only on customer-keyed readers (above).

**Codex pre-push round 10 (1 P0).** Pre-settlement dispute hardening: clearing the active PI for a not-yet-settled statement (1) stranded a `processing` ACH row (no PI ⇒ setup/reconcile/revert all refuse) and (2) removed the only PI→statement link before a `payments` row existed (so a later won couldn't restore). Now the not-yet-settled branch ALSO resets a `processing` statement to its prior payable status, and `handleDisputeCreated` INSERTS a durable disputed `payments` row (`status='disputed'`, keyed to the statement + PI + charge) when settlement hasn't written one — so `dispute.closed(won)` can find the statement and restore/settle the reinstated funds.

**Codex pre-push round 11 (2 P0 + 1 P1).** (1) **Atomic dispute reversal + durable row** — the pre-settlement PI-clear and the disputed-row insert now run in ONE transaction (`reverseStatementCascadeForDispute` accepts the caller's `trx`), so a row-write failure rolls back the PI-clear and the Stripe retry's PI lookup still finds the statement. (2) **`dispute.closed` reordered ahead of the row** — `handleDisputeClosed` now mirrors the PI-keyed statement lookup: a `lost` with no `payments` row reverses/blocks the statement + persists the durable disputed row; a `won` leaves the active PI for the eventual succeeded. (P1) **Stale `processing` events** — the statement `payment_intent.processing` branch re-reads the CURRENT PI status from Stripe and skips if it's no longer processing (a stale retry after failed/canceled would otherwise re-strand the statement).

**Codex pre-push round 12 (1 P0 + 1 P1).** (P0) **Late `dispute.created` after a won close** — the statement created branch now honors a recorded `dispute_final` marker (statement-scoped) and skips the reversal, so a reordered/retried created can't clear the PI + reopen children + undo reinstated funds after the dispute was won. (P1) the per-customer revenue breakdown's `whereNull('payer_id')` was unqualified and `customers` also has a `payer_id` column → ambiguous-column error; qualified to `payments.payer_id`.

**Codex pre-push round 13 (2 P0).** (1) **Full refunds reverse the statement** — `charge.refunded` only updated the `payments` row, leaving a fully-refunded statement + children `paid` (AR never recollects). Added a `payment.statement_id` + full-refund branch that reverses the statement cascade (PI-scoped, like the dispute reversal). (2) **Won-before-settlement ordering marker** — a `dispute.closed(won)` reordered before any `payments` row now persists a durable dispute-final marker keyed on the PI (so a late `created` skips reversal), and `settleStatementPaid` now UPSERTS its ledger row on the PI so the eventual `succeeded` consumes the marker (merging `dispute_final`) instead of writing a duplicate.

**Codex pre-push round 14 (2 P0).** (1) **Refund reordered before settlement** — `charge.refunded` (full) now resolves the statement by PI when no `payments` row exists yet, reverses the cascade + clears the active PI + writes a durable refunded marker, so a later `succeeded` can't settle refunded money. (2) **Won-restore surcharge validation** — `dispute.closed(won)` now re-applies a settlement directly ONLY when the row was already validated (`base_amount_cents` present); for a pre-settlement dispute MARKER it restores just the active PI and lets the eventual `succeeded` settle through the canonical `computeChargeAmount`/funding validation (so a base-only credit card can't become paid via won-restore).

**Codex pre-push round 15 — ARCHITECTURAL fix (owner-chosen): serialize the statement-money lifecycle.** Rounds 9–14 patched per-event webhook orderings (settle × dispute-created/won/lost × refund); the root cause was per-event mutation with pre-lock existence checks (TOCTOU). Introduced `withStatementMoneyLock(statementId, fn)` — a per-statement `pg_advisory_xact_lock` that `settleStatementPaid`, `reverseStatementCascadeForDispute`, `restoreStatementCascadeForDispute`, the succeeded handler, and every pre-settlement dispute/refund branch now acquire, so all money mutations for one statement are strictly serialized. The pre-settlement branches RE-CHECK the `payments` row INSIDE the lock (if settle won the race, mark the now-paid row refunded/disputed instead of inserting a stale marker). Two P0s closed by this: (1) a full refund racing settlement no longer leaves a paid row counted (in-lock recheck marks it refunded); (2) a `dispute.closed(won)` on a pre-settlement marker (which may have no future `succeeded` after `created→succeeded→won` orphaned it) is left for operator reconcile rather than marked paid (no stranded paid-row-vs-unpaid-statement).

**Codex pre-push round 16 (1 P0 + 1 P1).** (P0) the POST-settlement refund path's row update + cascade reversal also run UNDER `withStatementMoneyLock` now (a racing `succeeded` could otherwise flip the refunded row back to `paid` between the update and the reversal). (P1) the offline reconcile route now allowlists `check`/`ach`/`wire`/`offline` and rejects `card`/unknown — a `method: 'card'` would have recorded a card settlement at base with no surcharge, bypassing `computeChargeAmount`.

**Codex pre-push round 17 (1 P0 + 1 P1).** (P0) the pre-settlement refund guard now handles ANY refund, not just full — a PARTIAL `charge.refunded` before settlement was falling through to the 0-row generic update and being lost, so the later `succeeded` settled the full gross (overstating cash). Partial pre-settlement now persists a durable `stripe_orphan_charges` review item (full still reverses + marks). (P1) reconcile now takes the statement money advisory lock BEFORE the row `FOR UPDATE`, matching the webhook order (advisory → row), so a concurrent settle/refund/dispute can't deadlock with it.

**GitHub bot round 1 (1 P2).** Don't strand an ACH success on a transient lookup failure: `paymentDetailsFromIntent` defaults `paymentMethod` to `payment_method_types[0]` (= `card` for the dual card+ACH statement PI) when the charge/PM lookup fails, so the fail-closed-on-unverified-card-funding guard could orphan a legit ACH `succeeded`. Added a `resolved` flag (true only when method/funding came from actual Stripe data); the statement succeeded handler now THROWS on `!resolved` so Stripe RETRIES the webhook (the lookup almost always succeeds on retry) instead of guessing `card`.

**GitHub bot round 2 (1 P2 + 1 P3).** (P2) a statement `payment_intent.failed` that actually reverted a `processing` statement (a confirmed ACH debit that bounced days later, or a post-confirm card decline) now raises a durable admin notification — the silent revert left AP/operators no signal. (P3) the `/api/pay/statement` gate middleware now runs BEFORE the rate limiter, so a disabled `GATE_PAYER_STATEMENTS` always returns 404 (a 429 after 60 req/min would otherwise reveal the disabled surface exists).

**GitHub bot round 3 (1 P3).** Honor the "404 when off" contract even ahead of the GLOBAL `/api/` limiter: a pre-limiter gate at `index.js` 404s `/api/pay/statement` when `GATE_PAYER_STATEMENTS` is off, before the app-wide limiter can return a 429 to an IP that already exhausted it.

## 2026-06-21 — Third-party payer Phase 2 — P4 (AR + dunning) (feat/payer-statements-ar-dunning)

**Decision:** complete the NET-terms lane (after P1 accrual #1929, P2 close+deliver #1941, P3 pay+settle #1961 all merged dark) with the two pieces the statement model implies but nothing yet surfaces: **AR/aging keyed on the payer→statement**, and **statement-level dunning to the AP inbox**. Shipped dark behind `GATE_PAYER_STATEMENTS`, backend-first (matching P1–P3, which left the dedicated client statement UI to a later UI-consolidation slice). New: `payer_statement_followups` table, `server/services/payer-statement-followups.js` (dunning engine), `server/services/payer-ar.js` (aging), a dunning cron, admin AR + dunning-control routes, and a `get_payer_ar_aging` IB dashboard tool.

**AR / aging (`payer-ar.js`).** A NEW receivable layer — payer → statement → invoices — parallel to and independent of the per-customer/per-invoice self-pay AR (untouched). **Aging is keyed on the STATEMENT's `due_date`, never the child invoices'** (an accrued invoice has no individual due date; the statement is the receivable — hardest-integration-point #3 from the plan). Outstanding = `finalized | sent | viewed | processing` (`open` is still accruing, not yet a receivable; `paid`/`void` are settled). `processing` (payment in flight) stays an outstanding balance for AR even though dunning pauses on it — the money hasn't landed. Buckets by days-past-due (ET): `current (≤0) | b1_15 | b16_30 | b31_45 | b45_plus`. `summarize()` is pure (no DB) → reused by the per-payer read (`payerArForPayer`), the cross-payer "AR by terms" read (`computePayerArAging`, sorted oldest-past-due-first = the collections worklist), and the IB tool, so all three report identical numbers. Gate-dark safe: every read returns zeros until statements exist.

**Dunning (`payer-statement-followups.js` + config).** The statement mirror of `invoice-followups.js`, but **email-only to the payer's AP inbox — never the homeowner** (the P1–P3 invariant; the invoice followup engine already excludes payer invoices, so the two never overlap). Terms-aware cadence anchored to `due_date` (NOT sent_at — AP was already notified at close; dunning begins only once the NET window lapses): due+0 reminder / +15 firmer / +30 final. Anchoring to `due_date` makes it terms-aware for free (a net30 statement duns 15 days later in absolute time than a net15). ONE `payer.statement.followup` SendGrid template renders all three steps; the per-step tone rides a `reminder_line` config variable (no N-template sprawl). Unlike `payer.statement.sent` (no CTA), the reminder carries a pay CTA → the P3 `/pay/statement/:token` surface; the PDF is NOT re-attached (AP has it).

**Eligibility is driven off the STATEMENT, not the followup row** (`runPending` self-heals): a statement is dunnable while `status IN (sent, viewed)` and past due — the sequence row is created on first dun, so a send that never armed a row can't silently skip dunning. `processing`/`paid`/`void` are excluded by the status filter, so **settling a statement stops its dunning even without an explicit stop**. `viewed` does NOT stop dunning (AP opening the pay link without paying is exactly when we keep nudging — mirrors the invoice followups); only paid/void/processing pause it. One touch per statement per run; a hard delivery failure (incl. no AP email) pauses the sequence for operator attention rather than spinning. Per-(statement, step) idempotency key so a step never double-mails across overlapping ticks; the `runExclusive` cron lease is the outer guard. Cron: `15 10 * * 2-5` ET (staggered 15m after the invoice followups to spare the pool), gated — `runPending` no-ops when off.

**Settle → stop wiring.** `stopOnStatementSettled` is called best-effort OUTSIDE the money txn at both settle sites (Stripe webhook + admin reconcile) — it only tidies the row to `completed` (the eligibility status-filter is the real stop), and is wrapped so a dunning side-effect can never poison the settlement transaction or break on a pre-deploy missing table.

**Admin surface (`admin-payers.js`).** `GET /ar-aging` (cross-payer, registered BEFORE `/:id` so the literal path isn't captured as an id) + `GET /:id/ar` (per-payer outstanding + aging) + derived aging fields (`days_past_due`/`overdue`/`aging_bucket`) added non-breakingly to the existing `/:id/statements` rows. Dunning controls mirror the per-invoice ones: `GET .../followups` (sequence state) + `POST .../followups/:action` (pause | resume | stop | send-now), gated. IB: `get_payer_ar_aging` dashboard tool (read-only → not in write-gates) delegating to the same `computePayerArAging`.

**Schema.** `payer_statement_followups` — `statement_id` UNIQUE + ON DELETE RESTRICT (mirrors `invoices.payer_statement_id`; statements are voided, never hard-deleted), denormalized `payer_id`, status/step_index/touches_sent/next_touch_at + admin pause/stop columns. `payer.statement.followup` email template seeded via the same publish machinery as `payer.statement.sent`. Both ship dark; behaviour gated.

**Deferred (lane-consistent with P1–P3):** the dedicated client AR/statements/dunning page (the UI-consolidation slice — PayersPage still has no statement view), month-end auto-close cron, payer-portal statement view, PO enforcement, and the tech "Billed to … don't collect" banner (after the CompletionPanel rebuild). 20 new tests (`payer-ar.test.js`, `payer-statement-followups.test.js`); 81 payer tests green.

**GitHub bot round 1 (1 P2).** A dunning step whose email key was once suppressed came back from `sendTemplate` as `{ deduped: true, sent: false, blocked: true }`; `fireStep` treated any `deduped` as benign and ADVANCED `step_index` without delivering — silently skipping the reminder after a block. Fixed: `sendFollowupEmail` now classifies a dedupe as benign ONLY when it actually `sent` (already-delivered / in-flight-race winner); a blocked dedupe returns `{ ok: false, blocked }` so `fireStep` PAUSES instead of advancing. The explicit operator retry (`send-now`) now passes `forceRetry`, which walks past terminally-blocked generations to a FRESH key via the P2 `forcedRetryKey` (now exported from `payer-statement-email.js`) so a reminder whose key was suppressed can reach AP after the suppression is cleared — instead of deduping against the dead row forever. +2 regression tests (83 payer tests green).

**GitHub bot round 2 (1 P2).** The webhook `stopOnStatementSettled` ran unconditionally after the settlement txn, but that txn has anomaly paths that return WITHOUT paying (orphan/stale active-PI, unverified card funding, surcharge-mismatch quarantine) — so a non-settling success still completed the dunning row, halting collections on a statement that stays `sent`/`viewed` + unpaid. The txn now returns a `settledNow` boolean (true only on a fresh settle or an idempotent already-`paid`); the success log + dunning-stop fire ONLY when `settledNow`. The `!resolved` transient path still THROWS (Stripe retries), so it never reaches the stop either.

**GitHub bot round 3 (1 P2).** The dunning `EMAIL_SEND_IN_PROGRESS` race-loser returned `{ ok: true, deduped: true }`, so `fireStep` advanced `step_index` while the winning send was only `queued` — if that winner then failed (and auto-retries under the same key), the sequence had already moved past the step and the reminder was skipped. The loser now returns `{ inFlight: true }`; `fireStep` neither advances nor pauses on it (returns `reason: 'in_flight'`) so the step is re-evaluated next tick and only advances once it's genuinely delivered (`deduped && sent`) or freshly sent. +1 regression test (84 payer tests green).

**GitHub bot round 4 (1 P1).** The dunning email's "Pay this statement" CTA pointed at `/pay/statement/:token`, but the SPA has no public client route for it (only `/pay/:token`); P3 shipped the BACKEND `/api/pay/statement/:token` while the client statement-pay page remains the deferred payer-portal UI slice — so the CTA would dead-end at the authenticated portal catch-all (broken link). Dropped the online-pay CTA + `pay_url` from the `payer.statement.followup` template + engine payload (mirrors `payer.statement.sent`'s deliberate no-CTA stance); the reminder now asks AP to reply/call to arrange payment. The CTA + `pay_url` get re-added when the client statement-pay page ships (noted in the migration). 84 payer tests green.

## 2026-06-21 — Third-party payer Phase 2 — P5a (admin statements/AR/dunning UI) (feat/payer-statements-client-ui)

**Decision:** start the deferred client UI slice — the P1–P4 backend shipped the whole NET-terms lane but `/admin/payers` rendered only the list + edit form (PayersPage even still said statements were "coming in Phase 2"). This PR makes the lane **operator-usable**: the payer name now opens a detail Sheet with the statement lifecycle, dunning controls, and per-payer AR; a header "AR aging" button opens the cross-payer collections view. Read-only/no Stripe — the **public statement-pay page is split into P5b** so the money surface is reviewed on its own.

**`PayerDetailSheet.jsx`** (new, opened from the list): a Statements tab (each statement → status + aging badge, expandable to its visit lines + actions) and an AR tab (per-payer `GET /:id/ar` — outstanding, past-due, buckets). Statement actions map 1:1 to the P2–P4 endpoints: **Close & send / Close only** (`/close`), **Send / Resend** (`/send`), **Record offline payment** (`/reconcile` — method + amount mini-form), and **dunning controls** (`/followups/{pause,resume,stop,send-now}`) shown only for a dunnable (`sent`/`viewed`) statement or one that already has a sequence. **`PayerArAgingDialog.jsx`** (new): the org-wide `GET /ar-aging` — by-age + by-terms breakdowns and the oldest-first collections worklist; clicking a payer opens that payer's detail Sheet.

**Gate-dark safe:** the read endpoints return empty/zeros until `GATE_PAYER_STATEMENTS` is on (so the UI shows honest empty states today); the mutating actions surface the server's 403 ("not enabled") rather than faking success. Refreshed the stale "coming in Phase 2" copy in the edit form. Tier 1 V2 throughout (components/ui + zinc; `alert-fg` only on genuinely overdue amounts; type tokens limited to the defined scale). No local client build exists in-repo (client `node_modules` is empty; builds run on Railway) — verified by esbuild parse + full import-graph bundle-resolve instead.

**P5b (next):** the public `/pay/statement/:token` Stripe Payment Element page (no client route exists yet — only `/pay/:token`), which also restores the dunning email's online-pay CTA dropped in P4 round 4.

**Pre-push codex (2 P1, same PR).** (1) **Invalid reconcile amount → full-total charge.** A blank/NaN amount in the offline-payment form serialized to JSON `null`, which the server's reconcile treats as "default to the full statement total" — so a mistyped/cleared field would silently record the whole balance. `ReconcileForm` now validates a positive finite number client-side (disables Record + never submits NaN); the server still re-checks against the locked total. (2) **`paid_at` shown in UTC.** The settled timestamp rendered via the date-only (UTC) formatter, off by a day from ET after ~8pm; added a `dateInET` formatter (America/New_York) for TIMESTAMP columns while the DATE columns (period/due/service dates) keep the UTC date-only render.

**GitHub bot round 1 (1 P2).** The admin "Send to AP" button always posted `{}`, but a blocked/suppressed FIRST delivery leaves the statement `finalized` and `sendStatementEmail` only walks to a fresh retry key in `force` mode — so after AP fixes the bounce the button kept deduping against the dead blocked row and could never deliver. The button now posts `{ force: true }` for a `finalized` statement (safe — `forcedRetryKey` resolves to the stable base key when nothing's blocked, escaping only a real block) while a `sent`/`viewed` resend stays keyless (always re-sends).

**GitHub bot round 2 (1 P2).** "Close & send" finalizes the statement and then 422s when the AP delivery is blocked (response carries the frozen statement). The UI only showed the error and never refreshed, so the row stayed rendered `open` — leaving the operator with only "Close & send" (which reuses the first-delivery key and can't escape the block). `act` now refreshes on a partial-success error (a non-OK response that still carries `statement`), so the row flips to `finalized` and exposes the forced "Send to AP" retry.

## 2026-06-22 — Third-party payer Phase 2 — P5b (public statement-pay page + dunning CTA) (feat/payer-statement-pay-page)

**Decision:** ship the public `/pay/statement/:token` page (the money surface split out of P5a) so an AP contact can pay a consolidated NET statement online, and restore the dunning email's online-pay CTA that P4 round 4 dropped (there was no client page to point it at). The charge lands on the PAYER's Stripe customer; the statement settles to `paid` (cascading to its accrued invoices) via the Stripe webhook — the page only confirms the PaymentIntent.

**`StatementPayPage.jsx`** (new) + the `/pay/statement/:token` route in `App.jsx` (registered BEFORE `/pay/:token` so the two-segment path isn't shadowed; mirrors the server mount order). It mirrors PayPageV2's proven two-step surcharge flow — card: `elements.submit()` → `createPaymentMethod` → `/quote` → confirm → `/finalize` → `handleNextAction` on `requires_action`; ACH: `confirmPayment` direct (no surcharge) — trimmed of the invoice-only machinery the statement backend doesn't expose (no live `/update-amount` PI-reminting, no express checkout, no save-card/consent, no `/error` route). Customer-facing warm brand (WavesShell/BrandCard/BrandButton/SerifHeading), reusing the shared `getStripe` loader. On success it shows an inline "Payment received" state (statements have no `/receipt/:token` page). Gate-dark safe: a disabled `GATE_PAYER_STATEMENTS` 404s the backend, which renders the "couldn't find that statement" state.

**Dunning CTA restored.** New migration `20260622000003` re-publishes a new active version of the `payer.statement.followup` template WITH `pay_url` + the "Pay this statement" CTA (P4's `…0002` seeded it CTA-less); the engine (`payer-statement-followups.js`) supplies `pay_url = <portal>/pay/statement/:token` again (import + payload restored; test re-asserts the URL). 84 payer tests green.

**Verification:** no local client build in-repo (client `node_modules` empty; builds on Railway) — verified by esbuild parse + import-graph bundle-resolve (`@capacitor/*`/`@stripe/*` marked external). **The money page must be manually dry-run-tested before `GATE_PAYER_STATEMENTS` is enabled** (a real card + ACH through to a settled statement) — it can't be exercised in prod until the gate flips, so that test is the go-live gate.

**Pre-push codex (1 P0 + 1 P1, same PR).** (P0) **ACH could confirm a stale surcharged PI.** The card `/finalize` updates the shared PaymentIntent to base+surcharge before confirming; on a failed/abandoned card finalize the PI is left at the card-surcharged amount, and the page let the user switch to ACH (no surcharge) and confirm that same PI — charging the wrong amount and failing webhook amount-agreement. Fixed: every `handleFinalize` failure path now calls `onFinalizeFailed`, which resets the statement to a fresh BASE-amount PI by re-running `/setup` (its `requires_payment_method` reuse branch updates `amount` back to base + clears the surcharge metadata) before any further attempt. Quote/ACH failures don't reset (they never mutate the PI). (P1) **ACH billing details.** `us_bank_account` confirmation needs name + email; the statement Payment Element now seeds `defaultValues.billingDetails` from the AP contact (`billTo.company` / `billTo.ap_email`) so a bank-transfer confirm doesn't fail for missing details.

**GitHub bot round 1 (1 P2).** Handle Stripe redirect returns. An ACH bank-redirect (and 3DS) sends the AP contact back to `return_url` (`/pay/statement/:token?redirect_status=…`); the page just re-loaded + re-ran `/setup`, which 409s against the now-processing PI and showed a false "payment already in progress" error after a VALID redirect. Now `redirect_status` is read once on mount: a `succeeded`/`processing` return skips `/setup` and renders the "thank you — payment is in, receipt to follow" terminal state. Consolidated all success paths (inline confirm, redirect return, ACH processing, already-settled return visit) into ONE honest "submitted, receipt by email" state — it never claims "settled" while ACH is still clearing (settlement + receipt are the webhook's job).

**GitHub bot round 2 (2 P2 → one root fix).** The round-1 redirect handling trusted the `redirect_status` URL param unconditionally, so a stale/bookmarked return URL (e.g. reopened after an ACH failure that `revertStatementProcessing` flipped back to payable) would keep the statement pinned on the "submitted" terminal state and suppress the retry form. Replaced param-trust with **PaymentIntent verification**: Stripe appends `payment_intent_client_secret` to the return URL, so the page now `retrievePaymentIntent`s it and trusts the REAL status — `done` only when the PI is actually `succeeded`/`processing`, else `retry` (mint a fresh PI + show the form). A brief "Confirming your payment…" state covers the retrieve; the `/setup` effect waits for the verdict. Falls back to the param only if the retrieve itself fails. This fixes both the lag-window false error and the stale-param-pins-reverted-statement cases.

**GitHub bot round 3 (3 P2 → two refinements of the redirect verdict).** (a) **Verification failure must not trust the param.** If `retrievePaymentIntent` fails (Stripe.js blocked / offline / stale secret), the round-2 fallback still promoted `redirect_status=succeeded` to `done` — a bookmarked/tampered URL could fake success. Now a failed verification yields an explicit `unverified` state: it neither claims success nor re-mints a PI (which would risk a double-pay), and tells the AP "if you just paid you'll get a receipt — don't pay again; otherwise refresh." (b) **Processing terminal gated on the verdict.** `statement.status === 'processing'` was unconditionally terminal, but a failed-ACH return shows a lagging `processing` GET (until the webhook reverts) even though the retrieved PI already produced `retry` — so it falsely read as success. The `processing` terminal now applies only when the redirect verdict isn't `retry` (a genuinely `paid` statement stays terminal regardless). Dropped the now-unused `redirect_status` param read entirely — the retrieved PI is the sole authority.

**GitHub bot round 4 (3 P2 → bind the redirect verdict to this statement's active PI).** (a) **Bind to this statement** — verification trusted ANY retrieved PI that read succeeded/processing, so a stale secret from a since-refunded statement (or a copied secret on another statement's URL) faked success and hid the form for an unpaid statement. The GET now returns `active_payment_intent_id`; the page only honors a redirect as `done` when the return secret's PI is the statement's CURRENT active PI (else `retry` → form). (b) **Retry bypasses the lagging payable flag** — a verified `retry` whose statement GET still shows `processing` (webhook not yet reverted) used to fall into "Nothing to pay"; `/setup` now runs on a verified retry regardless of the stale `payable` flag (the backend is authoritative — it resets/mints a base PI, or 409s while genuinely processing, mapped to a plain "we're updating your statement, refresh shortly" message). The retrieved PI bound to the active PI is the sole authority; the persistent line-135 generic re-flag is resolved by this architecture.

**GitHub bot round 5 (1 real P2 + 2 false repeats).** Real: **strip stale Stripe params from `return_url`.** ACH `confirmPayment` used `window.location.href`, which on a retry from a bookmarked/failed return still carries the prior `payment_intent_client_secret` — so the next redirect comes back with TWO secrets and `URLSearchParams.get` reads the stale first one. The return URL is now `origin + pathname` (no query), so Stripe appends exactly one fresh param set. The other two flags ("handle redirect returns" / "bind to active PI") are re-posts of already-shipped logic — redirect returns are fully handled (verify → checking/done/retry/unverified) and `done` is gated on the return secret's PI being the statement's `active_payment_intent_id` (the binding check runs BEFORE the retrieve). Round-over-round re-flagging of the same shipped lines on this gated-dark page is the heuristic long-tail; the redirect handling is now architecturally complete (server-authoritative active-PI binding + clean return URL).

## 2026-06-24 — Dashboard: Net Momentum section (Core KPIs) (claude/dashboard-metrics-pest-lawn-deueg8)

**Decision:** add a "Momentum" section to the period-aware Core KPIs card on `/admin/dashboard` so the owner can see the period's growth STORY — customers and recurring revenue gained vs. lost — not just standalone levels. This is the "are we winning?" scoreboard number the existing dashboard lacked (it surfaced Active Customers + a Retention % but never net adds or net MRR movement). Content addition, not a visual refresh; strict Tier 1 V2 (components/ui + zinc; `alert-fg` only when a net is negative — a genuinely alert-worthy shrinking book).

**Backend** (`server/routes/admin-dashboard.js`, `/core-kpis`): added a `momentum` block to the response — `customers: {new, lost, net}` and `mrr: {new, churned, net}`. The **lost** side reuses the existing retention cohort (extended to also `SUM(monthly_rate)`, so `lostMRR = cohortMRR − retainedMRR` shares the SAME single "lost" definition as the count and the two can't drift). The **new** side reuses the canonical conversion-date source of truth (`member_since` in window via `CONVERSION_DATE_SQL` + `whereRealCustomer`), matching the headline "new this month" count. Net = new − lost — **no upgrade/expansion movement is inferred** (no clean source for it), so this is an honest new-vs-lost figure. Both queries wrapped in try/catch; a failure yields `momentum: null` and the section just hides.

**Frontend** (`DashboardPageV2.jsx`): a `Momentum` SectionLabel + two KpiTiles ("Net Customers", "Net MRR") at the top of the Core KPIs body, period-aware for free off the existing Today/WTD/MTD/YTD switcher. New `signed()` helper renders +gain / −loss / bare-0; each tile's sub shows the `+N new · M lost` breakdown; `alert` (red) only when net < 0. Renders only when `kpis.momentum` is present.

**Verification:** no runnable local stack in the fresh web container (DB migrations gated `predev`; client `node_modules` empty and a monorepo workspace pkg `@waves/lawn-cost-floor` isn't linked) — verified by `node -c` on the route, Prettier on the page, and a vite build that transformed all 2386 modules (incl. this page) before failing only on the unrelated unlinked workspace import. Live render not exercised.

## 2026-06-25 — Estimates: React redesign (PR B.2) becomes the default for new estimates — rollout Stage 2 (claude/quote-estimate-reversion-bltk3g)

**Context / why this came up.** The customer-facing one-time quote was reported as "looking like an old version." Root cause is the rollout state, not a regression: `/estimate/{token}` has two renderers — the legacy server-rendered HTML pipeline in `routes/estimate-public.js` and the React redesign (`pages/EstimateViewPage.jsx`, internally PR B.2). The gate (`estimate-public.js` `shouldUseReactEstimateView`) routes to React only when `use_v2_view===true || bill_by_invoice===true || cardHoldForcesReactView`. The `use_v2_view` column shipped **default false** (migration `20260423000002`, Stage 1: flip per-estimate via the `toggle_estimate_v2_view` IB tool). Separately, one-time-choice estimates (`show_one_time_option`) used to be force-routed to React because the mode toggle was "only implemented in the React view"; once the recurring/one-time toggle was rebuilt into the server-HTML `renderPage` (the `canChooseOneTime` branch, #2039) that forced route was removed so the rollout is governed solely by `use_v2_view`. Net effect: with the flag default-off, every quote (incl. one-time) served the legacy HTML — the "old version" the owner saw.

**Decision (Stage 2):** make the React redesign the default for **new** estimates. New migration `20260626000001_estimates_v2_default_on.js` flips the column DEFAULT to `true` via raw `ALTER TABLE estimates ALTER COLUMN use_v2_view SET DEFAULT true` (not knex `.alter()`, so it only changes the default for future inserts — no column rewrite, no nullability change, existing row values untouched). All six estimate insert paths rely on the column default (none set `use_v2_view`), so every newly-created estimate is now born `true` and renders in React; existing rows keep their stored value, so anything still at `false` stays on HTML (as the Stage-1 docstring promised). The per-estimate IB override still wins both ways. The gate is unchanged.

**Safe for one-time quotes:** `EstimateViewPage.jsx` has full one-time parity — `OneTimeModeToggle`, `OneTimePriceCard`, `serviceMode` recurring/one_time handling, structural-one-time forcing, and one-time card-hold/invoice — so defaulting one-time estimates to React is the richer experience, not a degradation. Stage 3 (backfill existing rows + remove the HTML path) remains a separate future PR.

**Codex review — React-default parity/exposure gaps.** Defaulting to React routes ordinary customer estimates through the SPA + its `/:token/data` and `/:token/accept` endpoints, surfacing pre-existing gaps vs. the legacy server-HTML page. Two small, verified ones are fixed **in this PR**; the rest are **split into a separate hardening PR** because they're security-sensitive (P1) and/or need a real-browser preview this container can't run.

Fixed here:
1. **noindex** — the legacy HTML set `<meta robots noindex>`, but the SPA fallback's `applySensitiveSpaHeaders` did not cover `/estimate/:token`, so React-served quotes (address + pricing behind a bearer token) became indexable. Added `isEstimatePath` to `server/utils/sensitive-spa-headers.js`. Estimate tokens come in two shapes — 32-hex (`randomBytes(16)`, admin) AND slug-style `${nameSlug}-${shortId}` (SMS/lead intake) — so rather than match a token shape (which would miss formats and leak, per a Codex P1), it noindexes ANY single-segment `/estimate/<x>` EXCEPT the known public marketing service slugs. Those slugs were extracted from `server/index.js` into a shared `server/config/service-estimate-slugs.js` (now `require`d by the index gateway too) so the privacy-header util and the `/estimate/:token` router agree on which URLs are public marketing vs. customer quotes. Over-noindexing a marketing page is a minor SEO cost; under-noindexing a real estimate leaks PII — so default to noindex. Test coverage added/updated.
2. **Expired-link view signals** — the legacy path short-circuits an expired link before any view tracking; the React `/:token/data` path reaches `shouldCountView`, which had no expiration guard, so opening an expired link fired a false view-count + status flip + admin "Estimate viewed" notify. Added the expiration guard centrally in `shouldCountView` (`expires_at < now && status !== 'accepted'`, mirroring `handleEstimateView`) so both the count and the first-view side effects skip expired links in both renderers.
3. **Uncacheable data payload** (Codex P2, post-merge sync) — the legacy `sendEstimatePage` HTML set `Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, must-revalidate`, but the React `GET /:token/data` JSON (address, phone/email, notes, pricing, bearer `askToken`) sent no cache/privacy headers. With React the default, that tokenized PII payload could be retained by shared browsers/intermediaries. Stamped `Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, must-revalidate` + `Pragma: no-cache` + `Referrer-Policy: no-referrer` at the top of the handler (every response path, incl. 404s) to match the legacy page.

Split out to the hardening PR (this default-flip PR must NOT merge ahead of it):
- **P1 — expired/draft data exposure.** `/:token/data` returns the full quote + customer phone/email/address/notes/pricing for **expired** estimates (only labels them `expired`), and both `/:token/data` and `/:token/accept` (`isEstimateAcceptActive`) treat a **null `expires_at`** as active and don't require *sent* status — so a leaked bearer URL for an expired estimate or a no-expiry draft (lead-webhook/agent inserts) can fetch the full payload or accept an unreviewed draft. Largely pre-existing on those endpoints; the default-flip widens it to every new estimate. Fix = enforce viewable preconditions (sent + non-expired, null-expiry = inactive) and redact non-viewable responses to a name+address expired shell.
- **P2 — accepted-estimate recap.** Showing the agreed services/pricing on a reopened accepted estimate (legacy parity) needs (a) the accepted *service mode* persisted/read so a mixed estimate's recap doesn't misrepresent recurring vs. one-time, and (b) the read-only recap to actually disable the add-on toggles (not just the frequency slider). Both are customer-surface changes that need a preview to verify, so they ride with the hardening PR rather than shipping blind here.

**Verification:** migration is `require`-clean and exports `up`/`down`; `sensitive-spa-headers` + `shouldCountView` guards unit-checked (9/9 spa-header tests green, expiration predicate verified). Scope of THIS PR: migration + the two server/header fixes above (no client changes). No `DATABASE_URL` in the container so the migration runs on Railway deploy (verify it ran post-merge); merge the hardening PR first so React-by-default never exposes the expired/draft payload. **(Update: the hardening PR #2089 merged first, as planned.)**

**Parity pass (post-#2089 merge) — remaining React-vs-legacy gaps Codex surfaced on the flip.** After #2089 landed and this branch was synced onto it, Codex flagged a cluster of behaviors where the React default diverged from the legacy HTML page; all closed here so the flip is clean:
- **Data payload now `no-store`** — the legacy `sendEstimatePage` set `Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, must-revalidate`, but `GET /:token/data` (address, phone/email, notes, pricing, bearer `askToken`) sent no cache headers. Stamped `no-store` + `Pragma` + `Referrer-Policy: no-referrer` at the top of the handler (all response paths).
- **Drafts stay on the legacy renderer** — with the flip, new drafts are born `use_v2_view=true`, but admin "Preview" opens the public `/estimate/<token>`, and the React `/:token/data` gate 404s drafts — breaking draft preview. The gate (`shouldUseReactEstimateView`) now `&& !UNPUBLISHED_ESTIMATE_STATUSES.includes(status)`, so `draft`/`scheduled` render server-HTML (preview works); the flip only takes effect once published. Keeps the #2089 security gate intact (a draft that reaches `/:token/data` still 404s).
- **No view-count inflation on refreshes** — `EstimateViewPage` re-fetches `/data` after preference/slot/accept actions; that endpoint counts a view on every 200, so toggling add-ons inflated `view_count` vs. the single legacy page load. The page now sends `?refresh=1` on every fetch after the first (tracked by a per-token ref), and the endpoint skips view-count + first-view side effects when present.
- **Accepted recap (the deferred P2, now built)** — `EstimateViewPage`'s `!canAccept` branch renders a read-only recap of the booked services + pricing below the accepted banner (legacy parity), via a shared `renderQuoteDetailCards(readOnly, modeOverride)` helper (single source of truth with the live configurator). Codex's two sub-issues are fixed: (a) **mode fidelity** — new migration `20260626000002_estimates_accepted_service_mode.js` persists the accepted mode at accept time (`accepted_service_mode`), surfaced as `acceptedServiceMode` and used to pin the recap, so a one-time acceptance on a mixed estimate isn't misrepresented as recurring (null for legacy rows → falls back to derived mode); (b) **read-only toggles** — `AddOnsBlock` gained a `disabled` prop (disables the checkbox + swaps the instructional copy) threaded through `ServiceSection`, so the recap's add-ons can't be clicked (which previously errored on `/preferences`).

**Parity-pass round 2 (Codex follow-ups on the parity pass — 3 P2).** (a) **Accepted frequency fidelity** — the recap seeded the recurring frequency from `section.defaultFrequencyKey`, so a customer who booked bi-monthly/monthly saw the default quarterly card/price. Added `accepted_frequency_key` to migration `…002`, persisted at accept (`acceptedFrequencyKey`), and `loadEstimate` now seeds `selected` from it for accepted rows — `selectedFrequency` + the combined price both derive from `selected`, so the whole recap follows. (b) **Resolved accepted mode** — `accepted_service_mode` wrote the raw request `serviceMode`, but a structurally one-time estimate commits as one-time even when the body omits it (`treatAsOneTime`); now persists `treatAsOneTime ? 'one_time' : serviceMode` so the stored mode matches the transaction. (c) **Refresh can't suppress the first view** — `?refresh=1` is a public param, so it's now honored only once `viewed_at` is already set; a caller hitting `?refresh=1` first can no longer suppress the initial view-count + admin "viewed" notification.

**Parity-pass verification:** server `node --check` clean; new migration (`accepted_service_mode` + `accepted_frequency_key`) + accept writes + payload fields present; `EstimateViewPage.jsx` + `AddOnsBlock.jsx` esbuild-parse clean; 9/9 header tests still green. **Still needs a Railway preview** (client doesn't build in-container): reopen an accepted one-time estimate → recap shows the one-time plan read-only (toggles inert); reopen an accepted **non-default-frequency** recurring estimate → recap shows the booked frequency/price; a draft `/estimate/<token>` still previews via legacy; toggling add-ons before accept registers one view, not several.

## 2026-06-25 — Estimates: harden the React data + accept endpoints for the React-by-default rollout (claude/estimate-react-endpoint-hardening)

**Context.** Prereq for making the React estimate view the default (companion to `claude/quote-estimate-reversion-bltk3g`). Codex flagged two P1 data-exposure gaps, largely pre-existing on these endpoints and widened by the default-flip: (1) `GET /:token/data` returns the full quote + customer phone/email/address/notes/pricing for **expired** estimates (only labels them `expired`); (2) both `/:token/data` and the accept/select-tier/preferences mutations treat a **null `expires_at`** as active and don't exclude unreviewed **drafts**, so a leaked bearer URL for an expired estimate or a no-expiry/lead draft could fetch the full payload or accept an unreviewed draft. The legacy server-HTML page short-circuited all of these (`new Date(null) < now` is in the past) to the expired/not-found shell before building any payload.

**Decision.** Add `isEstimateCustomerViewable(estimate)` and gate `GET /:token/data` on it: non-viewable → **404** (the SPA already renders its "this link may have expired or isn't valid" screen; no payload built). The signal is **status**, not a null expiry: unpublished states (`draft` — all six insert paths create rows as `draft` — and `scheduled`, which carries a *future* expiry until the send claim) are withheld, `expired`/`send_failed`/archived are withheld, `accepted`/`declined` are legitimate terminal views served in full (legacy parity), and `sending`/`sent`/`viewed` are served subject only to a real *past* expiry. **Admin previews bypass** (`hasAdminMarker` signed cookie / `isAdminIp`) so staff can still review drafts. Tightened `isEstimateAcceptActive` (shared by accept / select-tier / preferences) the same way: reject `draft`/`scheduled`. Status-based (not null-expiry) deliberately: a Codex P2 pass showed `sendEstimateNow` texts the link *before* writing `expires_at`, so a freshly-claimed `sending` row momentarily has a null expiry — a null-expiry-rejects rule would 404 the customer mid-send and broke an existing `isEstimateAcceptActive` test; gating on the unpublished `draft`/`scheduled` statuses closes the leaked-draft class without that fallout. Chose a 404 over a redacted 200 shell deliberately — it's leak-proof with zero render risk, vs. a shell whose render through the SPA's data contract I can't verify in this container; the slightly less branded "expired" screen is an acceptable trade for an edge/leaked-link case.

**Codex rounds 2–3 — admin bypass removed + TOCTOU (P1 + P2).** The first cut bypassed the viewability gate for `hasAdminMarker(req) || isAdminIp(ip)` so staff could preview drafts. Codex flagged this as too weak for releasing withheld PII: `isAdminIp` trusts a **spoofable `X-Forwarded-For`**, and the `waves_admin` cookie is a **2-year, logout-persistent** view-count marker — not authorization. An intermediate fix (`markerBelongsToActiveAdmin`: resolve the subject + require a currently *active* technician) revoked offboarded staff but **still** trusted a marker that survives logout on a shared device, and the public `/:token/data` fetch carries **no current-session credential** to check instead (the customer page sends no admin Bearer token). So the bypass was **removed entirely** — non-viewable estimates 404 for everyone; admin/staff preview of a draft or expired estimate must go through an authenticated admin surface, never this public endpoint. **Tradeoff flagged to the owner:** previewing a draft via the raw customer `/estimate/<token>` URL now 404s; a proper authenticated preview path is a follow-up if needed. Separately (P2 TOCTOU): the new draft/scheduled rejection only ran on the pre-read, so a customer with the page open could still win a race if an operator pulled the estimate back to `scheduled`; mirrored the unpublished guard into the four final-write `whereNotIn('status', …)` clauses (accept / select-tier / preferences / decline) so they now also exclude `send_failed`/`draft`/`scheduled`.

**Out of scope (deferred):** the accepted-estimate detail recap (Codex P2 — show agreed services/pricing on a reopened accepted estimate) needs the accepted **service mode** persisted (no column today; the accept path only echoes `serviceMode` in the immediate success payload) plus a read-only add-on-toggle fix — a separate cosmetic PR, since it needs a migration + a real-browser preview.

**Verification:** `isEstimateCustomerViewable` + the tightened `isEstimateAcceptActive` are unit-tested (`server/tests/estimate-public-viewability.test.js`, 11-row truth table verified inline; jest runs in CI where deps exist). `estimate-public.js` is `node --check`-clean. **Needs a Railway preview before merge** to confirm the integration edges this container can't exercise: a draft/expired token now 404s on the public link **for everyone (including staff)** — confirm office staff don't depend on the customer-URL draft preview (vs. the admin estimate page); a real expired customer link lands on the not-found/expired screen (not a blank); and a normal sent estimate still views + accepts. **Merge this BEFORE the default-flip PR** so React-by-default never serves the expired/draft payload.

## 2026-06-25 — Estimator: recurring spot-foam termite program + foam $250 floor removed (claude/recurring-foam-treatment-za7t6n)

**Context / why.** Two commercial clients independently asked for a recurring (~quarterly) spot foam treatment instead of repeated one-time calls. Owner directive: add a recurring foam option to the estimator at a per-visit rate discounted off the one-time price by cadence, AND remove the $250 foam minimum entirely (both one-time and recurring).

**Owner decisions (locked before build):** cadence ladder anchored on the one-time price — quarterly ×0.90 (10% off/visit), bimonthly ×0.85 (15%), monthly ×0.80 (20%); all three cadences offered; **standalone** — recurring foam does NOT count toward the WaveGuard tier and is not bundle-discountable (the cadence multiplier is its only discount); available to all customers; **$250 floor removed for all foam**. Note this differs from the pest-control frequency ladder (where quarterly is the 1.00 baseline and frequency buys the discount); for foam the one-time price is the anchor, so even quarterly is discounted.

**Foam is code-authoritative, NOT DB-bridged.** Unlike pest/lawn/mosquito/pre-slab, `db-bridge.js` (`syncConstantsFromDB`) never reads any foam key — there is no `config.foam*` handler and `validatePricingConstants` doesn't cover `foamDrill`. So foam's floor, margin, tiers, and the new recurring ladder live solely in `constants.js` + engine code and ship directly (the usual "editing constants.js is inert" warning does not apply here). No `pricing_config` migration was added — adding bridge machinery for foam would be a larger architectural change than requested, and the FM_CAN/FM_BITS rows in the legacy display table are unaffected.

**Pricing engine (server).** `constants.js`: `foamDrill.floor` `r(250)` → `0`; new `foamDrillRecurring { cadenceMultipliers, frequencies {quarterly:4,bimonthly:6,monthly:12}, defaultCadence:'quarterly' }`; added `foam_recurring` to `WAVEGUARD.excludedFromPercentDiscount`. `service-pricing.js`: dropped the `Math.max(floor,…)` in `priceFoamDrill`; new `priceRecurringFoam(points,{cadence})` returning a recurring line item (`service:'foam_recurring'`, `.annual`/`.monthly`/`.perVisit`, cost÷0.45 ×cadence, no floor). `estimate-engine.js`: new `services.foamRecurring` branch that pushes the line item but does NOT add to `activeServiceKeys` (so it can't create/raise a tier). Because it's a `.annual` line excluded from the % discount and not in `MANUAL_RECURRING_DISCOUNT_ELIGIBLE`, it sums into recurring totals at full cadence price with 0% discount automatically.

**Route + legacy mapper.** `property-lookup-v2.js` `translateV2CallToV1Input`: `sel.has('FOAM_RECURRING')` → `services.foamRecurring = {cadence, points}`. `v1-legacy-mapper.js`: added `foam_recurring` to `RECURRING_SERVICES` (so it isn't misclassified into one-time/specialty), and a `svcAdd('Recurring Foam …', foamRecLI, {discountable:false, countsTowardWaveGuardTier:false})` so it surfaces in `recurring.services`. Unlike palm/rodent it is NOT subtracted from `summary.recurringAnnual*`, so it correctly flows into `monthlyTotal`/year1/year2.

**Client.** `lib/estimateEngine.js`: removed `Math.max(250,…)` from one-time foam; new `svcFoamRecurring`/`foamRecurringFreq`/`foamRecurringPoints` fields; recurring foam compute block pushes to `wgServices` for display and into `ra`/`lineItems{discountable:false}` (NOT `ac`) so it joins the recurring monthly total without tier/discount; exposes `recurring.foamRecurringMo/Ann`. `EstimateToolViewV2.jsx` (live admin tool) + `EstimatePage.jsx` (retained V1 module; `EstimateToolView` is exported but currently has no importer — updated for parity): form defaults, the rough-preview memo (`separateRecurringKeys` + non-discountable approx), `selectedServices.push('FOAM_RECURRING')`, the `options` payload, and a "Recurring Foam Treatment" checkbox with Cadence + Drill Points selectors.

**Price effects.** One-time foam Spot $250 → ~$182 (floor gone); Moderate ~$308, Extensive ~$434, Full Perimeter ~$598 (now pure cost÷0.45). Recurring Moderate (10 pts): quarterly $277/visit ($1,108/yr), bimonthly $262/visit, monthly $246/visit.

**Verification:** server pricing checked via node (one-time floor removal + recurring ladder + standalone: pest+foam stays Bronze/serviceCount 1, foam line 0% discount); full server pipeline (`generateEstimate` → `mapV1ToLegacyShape`) confirms foam in `recurring.services`, `monthlyTotal`, year1, and never in one-time. 5-case client parity test (temp, since removed) matched server exactly. Jest: 694 pre-existing pricing/estimate tests green across 28 suites (incl. the client↔server drift parity suite); the relative-comparison foam tests still pass post-floor-removal. `vite build` compiles (EstimatesPageV2 incl. the new UI). Live render not exercised in-container (admin auth) — recommend a quick visual pass on `/admin/estimates` before merge.

### Round 2 (Codex review on #2092) — recurring foam lifecycle integration

Codex's review surfaced that the feature's footprint extends past the pricing engine into the estimate *lifecycle*. Owner approved going production-complete + auto-pricing commercial. Five downstream fixes:

- **Commercial auto-pricing** (`estimate-engine.js`, client `estimateEngine.js`): recurring foam now bypasses the `useCommercialManualQuote` safety gate and is priced at the cadence rate for commercial profiles too (the requesters are commercial). Deliberate exception — it's the first auto-priced commercial service; all others still route to manual quote. Verified: a commercial profile returns a `foam_recurring` line ($1,108/yr) with no manual-quote line.
- **Acceptance recurrence** (`estimate-converter.js` `supportsConverterFollowUpSeeding`, `recurring-appointment-seeder.js` `serviceKeyFor`): added a `foam_recurring` service-key rule (`/foam[_\s]*recurring|recurring[_\s]*foam/` — matches the recurring line + parent row but NOT the one-time "Drill-and-Foam Termite"), and allowed converter follow-up seeding for `foam_recurring` on all three cadences (quarterly/bimonthly/monthly). Without this, an accepted foam plan booked the first visit but `seedFollowUpsForParent`/`markParentRecurring` never ran, so it didn't recur. Pattern inference already worked off the "(Quarterly/Bimonthly/Monthly)" name + `visitsPerYear`.
- **Annual-prepay floor** (`estimate-converter.js` `nonDiscountableRecurringAnnualFloor`): the earlier `discountable:false` flag was insufficient — saved estimates persist the mapped `recurring.services` shape (no `lineItems`), and the floor only scanned `lineItems`. Now scans both sources (deduped by service key) and derives annual from `mo`/`monthly` when no annual field is present (new `recurringLineAnnualAmount` helper, also used by `isNonDiscountableRecurringLine`). Verified: foam-only floor = $1,108, so annual prepay can't apply the generic 5% on top of the cadence discount; a discountable pest line still yields $0 floor.
- **service_interest classification** (`estimate-service-lines.js`): added `foam` to the `termite` `SERVICE_LINE_PATTERNS` regex (+ `svcFoamRecurring` to the input-based path) so a foam-only recurring estimate classifies as `Termite` instead of `unknown` for follow-ups and admin lists. Verified.
- **Public customer estimate render** (`estimate-public.js`): added a `foam_recurring` category to `categoryForRecurringServiceKey`, label "Recurring Foam Treatment" to `serviceLabelForCategory` + `recurringServiceDisplayName`, and a warm-tone `SERVICE_COPY.foam_recurring` entry, so a foam-only customer quote renders as a foam section (was falling through to the Pest Control category/copy). `excludeFromPctDiscount` already resolves true via the constants exclusion.

**Verification:** 754 pricing/estimate/converter tests green across 31 suites (incl. commercial-safety-gate + prepay + parity drift); targeted node checks for all five fixes; client `vite build` clean. Customer-facing public render still needs a Railway preview (admin auth / no live stack in-container) before merge — confirm a foam-only quote renders under a "Recurring Foam Treatment" header with foam copy, and an accepted foam plan seeds future visits.

### Round 3 (Codex re-review on 7f1fce8) — public self-serve flow + booking

Codex confirmed the round-2 fixes resolved all prior threads and surfaced four more, all in the public customer estimate / self-booking flow. Three fixed; one deliberately skipped.

- **Engine-backed recurring allowlists** (`estimate-public.js`): added `foam_recurring` to both `RECURRING_LINE_SERVICES` sets (`recurringServicesWithSupplements` ~2168, `shapeFrequencyEntry` ~7885) and `RECURRING_SERVICE_KEYS` (~9585). Estimates saved via the engine-result path (not the v1 mapper) now surface foam as a recurring service for prepay eligibility, first-visit rows, and converter acceptance.
- **Cadence preserved through the public bundle** (`estimate-public.js`): the v1 bundle path fell back to `frequencies.slice(0,1)` (generic quarterly) for non-pest single services, so a bimonthly/monthly foam quote was presented and billed as quarterly. Added `foamFrequenciesFromV1Services()` — builds ONE frequency entry from the foam row's saved `cadence`/`visitsPerYear`/`monthly` (foam is an operator-chosen single cadence, not a customer-selectable ladder), billed monthly (annual/12), serviced at the cadence's visits/yr — and wired it into `buildPricingBundle`'s `finalFreqs` chain. The accept path reads this frequency unchanged, so `customerSelection.frequency`/billing now reflect the real cadence.
- **Booking slot sized from the foam tier** (`service-pricing.js` + `v1-legacy-mapper.js` + `estimate-slot-availability.js`): `priceRecurringFoam` now returns `estimatedDurationMinutes` (tier labor hours × 60 → 60/90/120/180), the mapper forwards it onto the recurring.services row, and `durationForService` has a `foam_recurring` case that uses it (clamped ≥60, ≤180) instead of the generic 45-min fallback — so a 10–20 point foam visit doesn't reserve a too-short slot.
- **SKIPPED — second foam pricer's $125 floor** (`calculateFoamPrice`/`services.termiteFoam`): verified `services.termiteFoam` is **not populated by any route or client**, so that spec-version pricer is dead in the live flow. Left untouched to avoid changing unrelated dead code; the owner's floor-removal directive targets the live drill-and-foam path, which is already floored at 0. Flagged for the owner — can zero it for consistency if desired.

**Verification:** 755 pricing/estimate/converter/slot tests green across 30 suites; full pipeline confirms the foam recurring row carries `cadence`/`visitsPerYear`/`mo`/`estimatedDurationMinutes` for all three cadences (quarterly 90min, bimonthly 120min, monthly 180min). The public self-serve render/accept/booking paths can't be exercised in-container (no DB/auth) — **needs a Railway preview**: send a bimonthly or monthly foam quote, confirm the customer page shows that cadence/price (not quarterly), accept it, and confirm the booking slot length + billing cadence are correct.

### Round 4 (Codex re-review on 7d6555d) — prepay mixed-plan split, engine-path cadence, client copy, sqft guard

Four more edge cases, all fixed:

- **Mixed-plan annual prepay split** (`estimate-converter.js` `resolveAnnualPrepayInvoiceTotal`): the round-2/3 `max(discounted, floor)` clamp only protected foam-heavy mixes. For foam + a discountable service (e.g. $1,108 foam + $600 lawn) the 5% was still computed on the whole base then clamped, bleeding part of the discount onto foam. Now the non-discountable floor is split out FIRST and added back at full price: `amount = floor + (base − floor) × (1 − rate)`. Verified: foam-only $1,108 (0% off), foam+lawn $1,678 (5% off the $600 lawn only), lawn-only $570 (unchanged). Updated `estimate-converter-prepay.test.js` (the prior assertion encoded the old clamp semantics).
- **Engine-invocation path cadence** (`estimate-public.js`): the round-3 foam cadence fix only ran in the v1 saved-estimate branch. Added `foamFrequenciesFromEngineResult()` (reuses `foamFrequenciesFromV1Services` against the engine result's `foam_recurring` line item) and wired it into the no-pest engine-invocation branch, so an `engineInputs`/`engineResult` foam quote at bimonthly/monthly isn't exposed as the default quarterly `FREQUENCY_LADDER[0]` (which also lacked `billingFrequencyKey: 'monthly'`).
- **Client React copy** (`client/src/lib/estimate-copy.js`): added a `foam_recurring` entry mirroring the server `SERVICE_COPY`, so the React estimate page header/AI panel (`estimateCopyFor(serviceCategory)`) no longer falls back to pest-control copy for foam-only quotes (the server already sends `serviceCategory: 'foam_recurring'`).
- **V2 estimator sqft guard** (`EstimateToolViewV2.jsx`): a foam-only quote was blocked by the "Enter home sq ft or lot size" dimension guard (only bed bug / pre-slab / Bora-Care were exempt). Recurring foam is priced from drill points + cadence, not footprint, so added a `foamRecurringOnly` exemption — operators can quote it before a property lookup.

**Verification:** 755 tests green across 30 suites (prepay split unit-verified for foam-only / foam+lawn / lawn-only); client `vite build` clean. Public self-serve render/accept still wants a Railway preview (unchanged from round 3).

### Round 5 (Codex re-review on 833eaa2) — engine-result cadence/duration/label polish

Three more, all in `estimate-public.js`, all on the engine-result ingestion + per-treatment rendering paths:

- **Cadence on engine-result supplements (P2)** (`recurringServicesWithSupplements`): a raw `foam_recurring` line item ingested here built a supplement row that dropped `item.cadence` and used the generic display name (no cadence), so on accept the seeder could fall back to the billing key `monthly` and seed monthly follow-ups for a quarterly/bimonthly plan. Now carries `item.name` (which holds the cadence) ahead of the generic name, plus `cadence`/`frequencyKey`/`estimatedDurationMinutes` on the row.
- **Tier duration in the foam frequency (P2)** (`foamFrequenciesFromV1Services`): the foam frequency object dropped `estimatedDurationMinutes` and emitted no `perServiceTreatments` row, but the slot profile reads `frequencies[].perServiceTreatments` first — so 15–20pt foam fell back to the generic 90-min window. Now carries `estimatedDurationMinutes` on the frequency and a `perServiceTreatments` row with the tier duration; `shapeFrequencyEntry`'s per-treatment rows carry it too.
- **Foam label on per-treatment rows (P3)** (`shapeFrequencyEntry.labelForRecurring`): added a `foam_recurring → 'Recurring Foam Treatment'` case (+ `li.name` fallback) so an engine-backed mixed estimate doesn't render a raw `foam_recurring` row. The client `PriceCard` renders `perServiceTreatments[].label` directly (no category-keyed benefit map needed).

**Verification:** 735 tests green across 29 suites; pipeline confirms the foam recurring row survives the supplement merge with cadence/visits/duration/name intact (bimonthly 20pt → 180min). Only `estimate-public.js` changed; no client rebuild. Public self-serve flow still wants a Railway preview.

### Round 5b (Codex re-review on 7b5f10d) — booking label + legacy V1 engine parity

(7b5f10d added the client foam benefit bullets in PriceCard via a parallel session; this branch was fast-forwarded onto it.) Three more:

- **Foam booking label (P2)** (`slot-reservation.js` `canonicalServiceTypeForProfile`): a foam_recurring profile had no case, so a booked recurring-foam accept took the coarse `service_interest` ("Termite") as `scheduled_services.service_type`, and the seeder copied that to follow-ups → Termite-labeled foam appointments. Added `foam_recurring → 'Recurring Foam Treatment'`. (Kept `service_interest='Termite'` as the high-level family — foam IS termite work — now that the booking label no longer derives from it.)
- **Foam-only legacy quote without sqft (P3)** (`estimateEngine.js`): the retained V1 client engine's size guard only bypassed `preSlabOnly`, so a foam-only quote returned "Enter home sq ft or lot size" before pricing. Added a `foamRecurringOnly` bypass mirroring the V2 estimator.
- **Foam row metadata in legacy engine (P2)** (`estimateEngine.js`): the client-engine `recurring.services` foam row omitted `cadence`/`estimatedDurationMinutes`/`discountable:false`, so a legacy-saved foam quote would lose cadence/duration and could stack the prepay discount. Now mirrors the server mapper's row (cadence, frequencyKey, estimatedDurationMinutes, discountable:false, countsTowardWaveGuardTier:false).

**Verification:** 325 slot/service-line/converter/public tests green across 12 suites; client `vite build` clean; a temp vitest confirmed the V1 engine prices a foam-only no-sqft quote and the row carries cadence/duration/discountable (bimonthly 20pt → 180min, discountable:false).

### Round 6 (06-26) — merge main + close the deferred foam floor

Merged `origin/main` (sole conflict: this append-only log — kept both the foam entry and main's invoice-AI entries; no code overlap, main touched none of the 17 pricing/estimate files this branch changed). Then **zeroed the residual `$125` floor in `calculateFoamPrice()`** (`service-pricing.js`), the spec-version `services.termiteFoam` pricer that round 3 deliberately SKIPPED. Re-confirmed it's dead in the live flow (nothing assigns `services.termiteFoam`; its only consumer `estimate-engine.js:1213` never fires; `PricingLogicPage` SpecServicesPanel only documents it), but zeroing its floor makes EVERY foam path consistent with the owner's "remove the minimum entirely" directive and closes the last open Codex thread. Kept `Math.max(0, …)` as a non-negative guard. 86 foam pricing tests green; no test asserted the old floor. **Still wants the Railway customer-render preview before merge** (unchanged from earlier rounds).

### Round 7 (Codex re-review on 268379bc0) — engine-backed foam accept (P1)

**Persist foam service rows for engine-backed accepts.** Codex found a real P1: quote-wizard (`public-quote.js` ~745) and IB agent-draft (`estimate-tools.js` ~481) estimates persist their priced lines ONLY under `estData.engineResult.lineItems` — there is no v1-mapped `result.recurring.services` row. The display path regenerates the foam frequency live (`foamFrequenciesFromEngineResult`) and exposes a sellable `monthly_total`, but the accept path builds `recurringSvcList` via `acceptanceServiceLists()` / `withSupplementedRecurringServices()`, and **those two functions read `estData.result || estData` — they omitted the `estData.engineResult` fallback that 6 other call sites in the same file already use** (e.g. `oneTimePestChoiceAmountForEstimate`). So a foam-only engine-backed accept locked `monthly_total` while `recurringSvcList` came back empty → `EstimateConverter` got nothing to schedule, seed, or invoice. Fix: both functions now source recurring rows from `estData?.result || estData?.engineResult || estData` (`withSupplementedRecurringServices` adds `recurringServicesWithSupplements(engineResult)` while preserving the `engineInputs`/`engineResult` wrapper so downstream pricing can still replay the engine). `recurringServiceKey('foam_recurring')` already returns `foam_recurring` and it's in `RECURRING_LINE_SERVICES`, so the stored line surfaces with service/name(cadence)/annual/monthly/visitsPerYear — enough to schedule + infer cadence + invoice. General fix (also covers any other engine-backed recurring line) but additive — the `result`-bearing v1-mapped path is unchanged. New `estimate-public-engine-foam-accept.test.js` (3) proves it: the 2 engine-backed assertions fail without the fix, the v1-mapped regression passes either way; +286 adjacent foam/pricing tests green.

**Follow-on (same round, found while verifying the P1 fix) — protect engine-backed foam from the annual-prepay 5%.** Surfacing the foam row as recurring makes a foam-only engine-backed estimate *prepay-eligible* for the first time — which exposed a latent gap: `isNonDiscountableRecurringLine` (the prepay-floor gate in `estimate-converter.js`) keyed only off the row's `discountable:false` flag, but `public-quote.js`/`lead-estimate-automation.js` persist `engineResult.lineItems` as a subset that DROPS that flag (and `estimateLineItemsFromData` reads `engineResult.lineItems`). So a foam line from those paths read as discountable → annual prepay would stack the generic 5% on foam, violating "the cadence multiplier is foam's only discount." Fix: `isNonDiscountableRecurringLine` now returns true for `recurringServiceKey === 'foam_recurring'` by service key (scoped to foam only — deliberately did NOT broaden to the whole `excludedFromPercentDiscount` map to avoid touching palm/rodent prepay treatment in this PR). New `estimate-converter-prepay.test.js` case (flag-less foam under `engineResult.lineItems`): floor = $1,108, foam-only prepay 0% off, foam+lawn discounts only the $600 lawn — fails without the fix, passes with it.

### Round 8 (Codex re-review on 931684a40) — compact-row cadence / annual / duration (3×P2)

All three stem from the same compact line-item shape (`public-quote.js` `engineResult.lineItems` map + `lead-estimate-automation.js` `compactLineItem`): `name`+`frequency` survive but `cadence` and `estimatedDurationMinutes` are dropped, and `annual` is the authoritative sold total alongside a rounded `monthly`. Now that round 7 surfaces these rows on accept, the gaps are live. Fixed at the source AND hardened the central consumer:
- **Cadence** (`foamFrequenciesFromV1Services`, used by the engine-result path too): defaulted any non-quarterly foam to quarterly when `row.cadence` was absent → wrong cadence on `/data` + accept selection. Now derives `row.cadence || row.frequencyKey || {4:q,6:bi,12:mo}[visits] || cadence-in-name` before the quarterly fallback (checks bi-monthly before monthly — "bimonthly" contains "monthly").
- **Annual** (same helper): recomputed annual from `monthly×12`, dropping cents (1108 → 1107.96) even though accept locks `selectedFrequency.annual` onto the estimate → invoiced a few cents under the engine price. Now prefers `row.annual ?? row.ann`, then `monthly×12`, then `perTreatment×visits`.
- **Booking duration** (`estimate-slot-availability.durationForService` foam branch): compact rows carried no `estimatedDurationMinutes`, so 15–20pt foam (120/180 min) fell to the 90-min default and self-booking could reserve a too-short slot. Fixed at the source: both compact mappings now carry `cadence` + `estimatedDurationMinutes` (generic, null for non-foam) — `priceRecurringFoam` already emits both, and `recurringServicesWithSupplements` forwards them onto the row. The 90-min foam default remains only for a genuinely-thin row.

Exported `foamFrequenciesFromEngineResult` for testing. Extended `estimate-public-engine-foam-accept.test.js` (now 6): cadence-from-visits/name (bimonthly 6→`bimonthly`, monthly 12 not misread as quarterly), annual preserved to the cent (1108 not 1107.96; perTreatment 277), slot duration 180/120 from the row + 90 default for a thin row. Cadence/annual assertions fail without the helper fix; +293 foam/pricing/slot tests green.

### Round 9 (Codex re-review on 177a9b7b3) — foam classification / mixed-pricing / annual / cadence-key (2×P1, 3×P2)

- **P1 — classify foam before sizing slots** (`estimate-slot-availability.js` `serviceKeyFor`): the foam duration branch only fired when the key was already `foam_recurring`, but an engine-backed row can reach slot sizing labeled only "Recurring Foam Treatment"/"FoamRecurring" (no mapped service key) → fell to the generic 45/60-min window, under-reserving 15–20pt (120/180-min) jobs. Added `/foam/ → 'foam_recurring'` (after the termite check so the one-time "Drill-and-Foam Termite" still maps to termite).
- **P1 — keep mixed foam estimates on full-summary pricing** (`buildPricingBundle` no-pest branch): `foamFrequenciesFromEngineResult` prices ONLY the foam line, so a foam + lawn/tree/mosquito mix would lock/prepay just the foam total and silently drop the other recurring service from the price (while still scheduling it). Now gated to **foam-only recurring mixes** (`recurringServicesWithSupplements(engineResult)` keys all === `foam_recurring`); any mix falls through to the full-summary `shapeFrequencyEntry`. Verified: foam+tree prices the combined annual ($1,595) with both services in `perServiceTreatments`, not the $1,108 foam-only total.
- **P2 — foam annual on the mapped row** (`v1-legacy-mapper.js` foam `svcAdd`): the admin/V2-mapped row carried `mo`/`perTreatment` but not the engine `annual`, so `foamFrequenciesFromV1Services` fell back to `monthly×12` (1108 → 1107.96 on accept/prepay). Now carries `annual: Number(foamRecLI.annual)`.
- **P2 — normalize the cadence key** (`priceRecurringFoam` + `foamFrequenciesFromV1Services`): both only recognized `bimonthly`, but the billing/estimate stack also uses `bi_monthly`; a `{cadence:'bi_monthly'}` caller/replay silently fell back to quarterly (4 visits at the quarterly multiplier instead of the 6-visit bimonthly). Added a `bi_monthly`/`bi-monthly`/`bimonth → bimonthly` alias normalization before each lookup; in the frequency helper the normalization also stops an alias-form `row.cadence` from short-circuiting the derive chain.

Extended `estimate-public-engine-foam-accept.test.js` (now 12): foam-by-name slot classification + termite-still-termite, `priceRecurringFoam`/`foamFrequenciesFromEngineResult` bi_monthly→6-visit, `buildPricingBundle` foam-only vs foam+tree full-summary, mapped foam row annual=1108. All 5 fail without their fix; +334 foam/pricing/slot/converter tests green.

### Round 10 (Codex re-review on c4170e368) — engineInputs-only accept / mixed cadence / cent-exact annual (1×P1, 3×P2)

- **P1 — persist generated foam rows for engineInputs-only accepts** (`withSupplementedRecurringServices`): round 7 read `result || engineResult`, but an estimate stored with ONLY `engineInputs` (a supported display path — `buildPricingBundle` replays the engine) has neither, so accept got an empty recurring list → locked total, no schedule/seed/invoice. Now when no recurring rows are found and there's no `result`/`engineResult`, it replays `generateEstimate(extractEngineInputs(estData))` and supplements from that (engine wrapper preserved; `generateEstimate` already imported).
- **P2 — keep foam cadence in a mixed plan** (`shapeFrequencyEntry` per-service-treatment rows): the round-9 fix routes a foam + lawn/tree/mosquito mix through the full-summary entry whose top-level key is the generic quarterly ladder row. Added `cadence`/`frequencyKey` to each per-service-treatment row so foam's own cadence (e.g. bimonthly, 6 visits) survives on its row even when the bundle header is nominal — scheduling/seeding read it per-service.
- **P2 (Codex) — foam cent-exact in mixed V1/admin bundles** (`shapeFromV1`): Codex flagged that summing `svc.mo` then `×12` locks a foam-in-mix portion at `92.33×12 = 1107.96` vs the engine's `1108`. **Owner directive 2026-06-26: cent-exactness is NOT required** — so the foam-scoped `shapeFromV1` correction (and its test-only `shapeFromV1` export + test) was **reverted**. A foam-in-mix bundle now totals `mo×12`, consistent with how every other recurring service is bundled; the ~4¢ delta is accepted.
- **P2 — exact annual on the client foam row** (`client/src/lib/estimateEngine.js`): KEPT — the legacy client-saved `recurring.services` foam row now carries the already-computed `ann` (`annual: ann, ann`). This isn't "chasing cents": it just passes through the value the engine computed, so the common **foam-only** path (via `foamFrequenciesFromV1Services`, which prefers `row.annual`) shows the natural round `$1,108` with zero core-function risk. (Mixed bundles still use `mo×12` per the revert above.)

`estimate-public-engine-foam-accept.test.js` now 14: engineInputs-only replay surfaces foam on accept (+ wrapper kept) and foam-in-mix treatment row keeps `cadence:'bimonthly'`. The P1 + the two structural P2 assertions fail without their fix; foam/pricing/slot/converter/drift suites green (client `annual` leaves the client↔server drift parity green).

### Round 11 (Codex re-review on 7ca266c52) — engineInputs-only foam section labeled Pest Control (P2)

The round-10 accept fix (`withSupplementedRecurringServices` engine replay) covered the ACCEPT path, but the DISPLAY path had the same gap: for an engineInputs-only foam quote, `buildPricingBundle` builds the foam-specific frequency but `buildPricingServices` reads the static estData (no recurring rows) and falls to `deriveServiceCategory(estData, [], [])`, whose engineInputs **inference fallback recognized pest/lawn/tree/mosquito/termite/etc. but not `services.foamRecurring`** → defaulted to `'pest_control'`, so `/api/estimates/:token/data` (and its section) labeled a foam quote as Pest Control. Fix: added `services.foamRecurring || inputs.svcFoamRecurring → 'foam_recurring'` to the inference list (one line, mirroring the existing per-service entries). This fixes both the `/data` top-level `serviceCategory` (drives the React copy via `estimateCopyFor`) and the empty-recurringKeys section fallback (`buildServiceSection` key/label) — zero impact on other estimate types (foam was the only service missing from the inference). Chose this over supplementing estData with the regenerated engineResult (which would change `recurringServices` for ALL engineInputs-only estimates). Tests: `deriveServiceCategory(engineInputs-only foam, [], []) === 'foam_recurring'` + the `buildPricingBundle` section labels foam (both fail without the fix); 314 foam/pricing/converter/drift tests green.

## 2026-06-25 — Invoices: one-tap AI invoice summary from the linked visit (feat/invoice-ai-summary)

**Context.** The admin invoice builder already had a "Write with AI" button that drafted the customer-facing invoice note, but it only saw what the operator typed plus the line-item descriptions — it had no idea what actually happened at the visit. Most invoices are created against a completed `service_records` row (the operator picks the service), so the richest context (the tech's job summary, the diagnostic readings captured on the form) was sitting one join away and going unused. This makes the AI note ServiceTitan-style: a one-tap summary assembled from the visit, not just from re-typed line items.

**Decision.** Extract the note generation out of the route into a dedicated service (`server/services/invoice-ai-summary.js`) and feed it the linked visit. `POST /api/admin/invoices/notes/ai` now accepts `serviceRecordId` + a `sources` toggle object (`{ jobSummary, forms, lineItems }`) on top of the existing `input` + `services`; the service loads the `service_records` row and assembles the prompt from three sources mapped to the UI toggles — `jobSummary → technician_notes`, `forms → soil/lawn diagnostic readings`, `lineItems → invoice line descriptions`. Back-compatible: with no `serviceRecordId` the old typed-input + line-items path is unchanged, so the base button keeps working everywhere.

**Model tier.** Customer-facing copy → `MODELS.VOICE` (Sonnet, warm/natural), matching `completion-recap.js`, **not** the old `MODELS.FLAGSHIP` this endpoint used (a stray flagship call site for what is plainly customer-voice copy). The now-unused `MODELS` import was dropped from the route.

**Guardrails** mirror `completion-recap.js`: never names products / chemicals / active ingredients / application rates / prices, never says "eliminated/guaranteed/pest-free/eradicated/solved forever", invents no follow-up dates or pests, and never emits raw field codes or internal QA flags (`field_flags` is deliberately excluded from `formatObservations`; readings are translated to plain language). Degrades gracefully — a missing/failed `service_records` lookup returns an empty context (logged `warn`) so the operator's typed input + line items still drive generation rather than 500-ing.

**Summary reaches the customer in the email body.** `sendInvoiceEmail` previously only put the note on the attached PDF.
