It now surfaces `invoice.notes` as a rendered, HTML-escaped paragraph in the email body (both the HTML and plain-text branches) and as an `invoice_summary` SendGrid merge variable. **Ops prerequisite / soft prod gate:** prod disables SMTP fallback and sends via the SendGrid `invoice.sent` template, so the summary only appears in the prod email once that template renders the new `invoice_summary` merge field — until then the prod email is unchanged (safe, gradual rollout). Dev/staging SMTP shows it immediately.

**UI.** `AdminInvoicesPage.jsx` `CreateInvoice` (legacy `D` palette — matched the file). Flag-gated on `ff_invoice_ai_summary` (off by default; fails closed). When the flag is on and a completed visit is linked (`selectedService?.id` in create mode, `editInvoice.service_record_id` in edit mode), it renders "Pull from visit" checkboxes (Job summary / Field observations / Line items) and sends `serviceRecordId` + `sources`; the button label flips to "Rewrite with AI" once a draft exists. With the flag off, behavior is identical to before.

**Verification.** `server/tests/invoice-ai-summary.test.js` (7) + `server/tests/invoice-email-summary.test.js` (3) green; existing `AdminInvoicesPage.test.jsx` (6) still green. No-overlap rebase onto `origin/main`. `notes/ai` still hard-requires `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`.

**Codex round 1 (5 findings, all addressed).**
- **P1 — cross-customer visit leak.** `loadServiceContext` fetched the visit by `id` only; the builder doesn't clear `selectedService` when the operator switches customers, so a stale `serviceRecordId` could draft another customer's technician notes into this invoice. Now scoped: `loadServiceContext(serviceRecordId, customerId)` requires BOTH and queries `where({ id, customer_id })`, **failing closed** if `customerId` is absent (mirrors the ownership join invoice creation already enforces). The `/notes/ai` client now sends `customerId`, and selecting a new customer clears `selectedService`/`serviceRecords` (defense in depth).
- **P2 — summarizing a not-yet-performed visit.** The picker returns records of any status. `loadServiceContext` now only treats `PERFORMED_STATUSES` (`completed`/`paid`) as usable; a `scheduled`/`pending`/`void` record yields empty context.
- **P2 — `invoice_summary` not renderable in prod.** Prod sends via the SendGrid `invoice.sent` template (SMTP fallback disabled), which neither rendered `{{invoice_summary}}` nor whitelisted it (the publisher rejects referenced-but-unallowed vars). New migration `20260626000006_invoice_sent_render_summary.js` re-publishes invoice.sent with a `callout` block for `{{invoice_summary}}` (after the greeting, above the details table) + adds the variable to allowed/optional + seeds the fixture. Loads the CURRENT active version (no hardcoded blocks) and is idempotent. The renderer suppresses empty blocks, so summary-less invoices are unchanged.
- **P2 — free-form note tripping the placeholder guard.** `sendTemplate` runs `productionPlaceholderPayloadValues` over every payload value; a legitimate summary like "Sample collected…" matches the `^sample` placeholder pattern and would fail the send. Added a `FREE_FORM_PAYLOAD_KEYS` exemption (`invoice_summary`) in `email-template-library.js`.
- **P3 — generating from only a visit label.** `hasUsableContext` treated `context.serviceType` as usable even with every source toggle off; removed that branch so a summary needs typed input or an enabled source with data.

**Codex round 2 (1 finding, addressed).** **P1 — template version-number collision.** Migration `…0006` derived the new version number from the *active* row, but an unpublished `invoice.sent` draft can already hold `active.version_number + 1`, and `(template_id, version_number)` is unique — so the migration would collide and abort the deploy. Now numbers from the LATEST version across ALL statuses (`MAX(version_number) + 1`), matching the existing publish path. (Same fix applied to `…0007` on #2109.)

## 2026-06-25 — Invoices: AI thank-you message in the invoice email (feat/invoice-email-message, stacked on feat/invoice-ai-summary)

**Context.** Follow-up to the one-tap invoice summary. The summary recaps *what was done* at the visit (and prints on the PDF). This adds a distinct, optional **personal thank-you message** that lives only in the invoice **email** — a relationship note ("thank you for trusting us…"), not a work recap. Chosen over reframing the auto-intro because the owner wanted a separate, operator-editable note rendered alongside the summary (email layout: auto greeting → service summary → thank-you message → line-item table → pay CTA).

**Schema.** New nullable `invoices.email_message` column (migration `20260626000005_invoices_email_message.js`). Deliberately separate from `notes`: `email_message` is email-only and **never** placed on the PDF. Existing rows stay null; the email renders exactly as before when empty.

**Generation.** New `generateThankYouMessage` / `buildThankYouPrompt` in `invoice-ai-summary.js` (reuses the same VOICE-tier call + guardrails). Distinct prompt: 1–2 sentences, warm/appreciative, **no greeting** (the email already opens with "Hi {first}"), and the same no-products / no-prices / no-overpromising rails as the summary. New endpoint `POST /api/admin/invoices/email-message/ai` (`{ customerName, serviceType, input }`), hard-requires `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`; returns a friendly error (never a 500) when AI is unavailable.

**Persistence.** `email_message` threads through `InvoiceService.create` (new `emailMessage` arg → `email_message` column) and the PUT edit path via the `INVOICE_UPDATE_ALLOWED_FIELDS` allowlist — `email_message` added alongside `notes`/`title` (it is plain customer-facing text, NOT a money/status column, so it respects the audit invariant; the `stripe-payments.test.js` exact-shape assertion was updated to match).

**Send wiring.** `sendInvoiceEmail` renders `invoice.email_message` as its own paragraph **after** the service summary and **above** the line-item table (HTML + plain-text), and passes it as an `invoice_message` SendGrid merge variable. Rendered as a plain paragraph (no info-card chrome) so it reads as a personal note, visually distinct from the boxed summary above it. Same prod gate as the summary: the in-body message only appears in the prod email once the SendGrid `invoice.sent` template renders the new `invoice_message` field; dev/staging SMTP shows it immediately.

**UI.** `AdminInvoicesPage.jsx` `CreateInvoice` (legacy `D` palette). Flag-gated on a NEW flag `ff_invoice_email_message` (off by default, fails closed — independent of `ff_invoice_ai_summary`). Adds an "Email thank-you (optional)" field with its own Write/Rewrite-with-AI button and a hint clarifying it shows in the email, not the PDF; works in create + edit mode (prefilled from `editInvoice.email_message`, which is present because the list query selects `invoices.*`).

**Verification.** New `invoice-thank-you.test.js` (4) + `invoice-email-thank-you.test.js` (3); updated `stripe-payments.test.js` allowlist assertion; `invoice-ai-summary` (7) + `invoice-email-summary` (3) + `AdminInvoicesPage.test.jsx` (6) still green — 82 server tests across the affected suites pass. All changed server files `node --check`-clean. **Stacked PR:** based on `feat/invoice-ai-summary` (#2107); retarget to `main` (rebase, dropping the merged summary commit) once #2107 lands. **UI not yet rendered in a real browser** — flag is off by default and needs a `user_feature_flags` row to surface; recommend a render check before flipping `ff_invoice_email_message`.

**Codex round 1 (1 finding, addressed).** **P2 — `invoice_message` not rendered in prod.** Like the summary, the thank-you note only existed in the SMTP-fallback HTML (disabled in prod). New migration `20260626000007_invoice_sent_render_message.js` re-publishes `invoice.sent` with a plain paragraph block for `{{invoice_message}}` placed directly AFTER the summary callout (greeting → summary → thank-you → details → CTA) + whitelists the variable + seeds the fixture; loads the CURRENT active version so it composes with `…0006` (the summary block) regardless of run order, and is idempotent. Also added `invoice_message` to `FREE_FORM_PAYLOAD_KEYS` in `email-template-library.js` (same placeholder-guard exemption the summary got in #2107) so a thank-you note that happens to start with "Sample…" can't fail the send. This **closes the soft prod gate** the original entry described — both summary and message now render in the prod template once `…0006`/`…0007` deploy.

## 2026-06-26 — PPC offline conversions: automate the existing Data Manager uploader + make call leads visible in the funnel (feat/ppc-call-attribution-dm-cron)

**Context / course-correction.** The original task was "upload offline conversions back to Google Ads + attribute phone-call leads." A first pass built a NEW queue + funnel hooks + an uploader on the Ads API `ConversionUploadService` — which a live validate-only test proved is **deprecated for new accounts** (`"limited to existing users… use the Data Manager API"`). It also turned out the repo **already had a complete Google Data Manager API uploader** (`server/services/ads/data-manager.js`, PR #1730): pull-based qualified-lead (from `leads`, incl. hashed email/phone = Enhanced Conversions for Leads, which already covers phone-call leads) + completed-job-revenue (from `estimate_actuals` + invoice totals), wired to `routes/admin-analytics.js`, logged to `google_ads_conversion_uploads`, service-account auth, and already configured LIVE in prod (`GOOGLE_DATA_MANAGER_ALLOW_UPLOADS=true`, `VALIDATE_ONLY=false`). The discarded first pass was redundant. This entry is the corrected, minimal scope.

**Decision 1 — automate the existing uploader.** `data-manager.js` was **admin-trigger only** (no scheduler). Added a daily 6:40am ET cron in `scheduler.js` that calls `DataManager.uploadConversions` for both conversion types (`periodDays: 7`, `limit: 500`, `validateOnly: false`). Safety: it no-ops unless `GOOGLE_DATA_MANAGER_CRON_ENABLED === 'true'` (opt-in so it never auto-fires on deploy), it's double-gated under the existing `cronJobs` wrapper, and `uploadConversions` still enforces the module's own `ALLOW_UPLOADS`/`VALIDATE_ONLY` gating (validate-only unless the account is explicitly live) and de-dupes per `transaction_id`, so the 7-day re-scan never double-reports. No change to `data-manager.js` itself. Documented the (previously undocumented) DM env vars in `.env.example`.

**Decision 2 — call leads visible in the PPC funnel.** The DM uploader feeds Google, but the `/admin/ppc` ROI views read `ad_service_attribution`, which only the web `lead-webhook.js` ever wrote — so inbound calls were invisible there. New `services/ads/call-attribution.js` `recordCallPpcAttribution()` inserts an `ad_service_attribution` row (`funnel_stage='lead'`, `lead_source='google_ads'`, `campaign_id` resolved from the campaign Google's call-reporting bridge matched), idempotent per `(customer_id, lead_source, lead_date)`. Wired into `google-call-bridge.applyBridge` (per-campaign, on the main line today) and `call-recording-processor.js` lead creation (dedicated GA tracking number → single-number bucket, `campaign_id` null, per-campaign-ready). Fire-and-forget; never blocks call processing.

**Verification.** New `ads-call-attribution.test.js` (13); existing `google-call-bridge` (12) + `data-manager` suites still green; changed files `node --check`-clean. Created one live conversion action during investigation — `Waves - Booked Job` (`…/7662382463`, BOOK_APPOINTMENT) — currently UNUSED by the 2-type DM uploader (harmless; removable, or wire a third type later). **Owner to go live on automation:** set `GOOGLE_DATA_MANAGER_CRON_ENABLED=true` (the DM account is already configured for live uploads).

**Codex round 1 (5×P2, all addressed).** Campaign backfill on an existing null-campaign attribution row (dedicated-number path then bridge); `findLeadForCall` returns the matched lead's `customer_id` so phone-matched leads attribute; pass extracted `serviceInterest` + the actual call date into `recordCallPpcAttribution` (service-line ROI + stable idempotency key for replays); wrap the upload cron in `runExclusive` (no double-POST across pods/deploys).

**Codex round 2 (3×P2, all addressed).** (1) Attribute in the bridge's already-bridged branch too (shared `writeCallPpcAttribution` helper) so calls bridged before this shipped + lead-retry calls land in the funnel (idempotent). (2) New `DataManager.reconcilePendingRequests()` + the cron reconciles prior runs' still-pending request IDs first, so failed/partial uploads flip out of `pending` and become retryable instead of stuck forever. (3) Wider cron window dated by `COALESCE(converted_at, first_contact_at, created_at)` — qualified_lead 60d / completed_job_revenue 30d — to catch late-qualified leads before Google's ~90d import window closes.

**Codex round 3 (2×P2, all addressed) — "attribute actual leads only".** (1) `writeCallPpcAttribution` now requires a `leadId`, not just a `customerId` — a confirmed Google Ads call from an EXISTING customer that matched no lead (a service/support call) is no longer counted as a new PPC lead, mirroring the lead-creation gate in call-recording-processor. (2) In call-recording-processor the lead-source lookup was hoisted to run for BOTH the new-lead and existing-lead paths, and the attribution write moved after the if/else (gated on `leadId`) — so a paid tracking-number call that matches a REUSED lead by phone is now recorded too, instead of only brand-new-lead inserts.

**Codex round 8 (2×P2, all addressed).** (1) The web-owned guard now also covers UTM-only web rows (no click id) — `utm_campaign`/`utm_term` join gclid/wbraid/gbraid, so a later call can't overwrite a consent/ad-blocker web lead's first-touch campaign (reason renamed `web_attributed`). (2) Widened the qualified-lead cron window 60→90 days (the full Google import window) so a lead first contacted up to 90 days ago but qualified only now (is_qualified set without converted_at → dated by first_contact) is still uploaded; anything older is outside Google's window regardless.

**Codex round 7 (3×P2, all addressed) — keep attribution clean + correct.** (1) The dedicated-number path now gates on `source_type === 'google_ads'` (not any `channel='paid'`), so a Facebook/LSA/other paid tracking number isn't mislabelled as a Google Ads call. (2) Call attribution returns `click_attributed` (no insert/override) when the lead's existing row carries a click id (gclid/wbraid/gbraid) — a web-form Google Ads lead's first-touch campaign is no longer clobbered when the customer later phones a paid number. (3) The bridge's already-bridged backfill + retry now only write PPC attribution when the CRM call's `google_ads_call_resource_name` equals THIS `match.googleCall.resourceName` — a call that scored 'already_bridged' off a different nearby Google call no longer gets that other call's campaign (lead-attribution retry, which is campaign-agnostic, still runs).

**Codex round 6 (1×P2, addressed) — upgrade placeholders, not just nulls.** The backfill only filled NULL fields, but the dedicated-number path always inserts a row with a generic `lead_source_detail` ("inbound call") + default service bucket, so a later bridge run (real campaign + a now-known service on the lead) never replaced them. Now: when the bridge first supplies a campaign (`campaign_id` null → set), the generic detail is replaced with the campaign name; and a service derived from a KNOWN interest upgrades a default-placeholder bucket (an unknown/default inference still only fills missing fields). An already-set `campaign_id` is never overwritten with a different one (first-touch wins).

**Codex round 5 (3×P2, all addressed) — dedupe robustness.** (1) `ad_service_attribution.lead_id` is now a UNIQUE index (migration `…0013`) + the call/web inserts use `ON CONFLICT (lead_id) DO NOTHING`, so two overlapping bridge-apply runs can't both insert a row for the same lead (Postgres NULLs-distinct leaves the many null-lead_id web rows unaffected). (2) The advisory lock moved INSIDE `DataManager.uploadConversions` (per-conversion-type) so the manual `/data-manager/upload` admin endpoint is serialized with the cron too (the cron's redundant outer lock was removed; reconcile stays outside). (3) The web attribution insert now stamps `lead_id`, and call attribution returns `other_source` (no insert, no override) when a lead already has a row under a different source — so a customer who fills the web form and then calls the paid number is counted once under the web source, not double-counted.

**Codex round 4 (4×P2, all addressed) — funnel data quality.** (1) Root fix: new `ad_service_attribution.lead_id` column (migration `20260626000013`) — call attribution now dedupes by **lead_id** (one row per lead) instead of the coarse (customer, source, day) key, so two distinct Google Ads leads for one customer on the same day (web form + phone call, or two calls) get distinct rows. (2) Extracted the web path's `inferServiceLine`/`inferSpecificService`/`inferServiceBucket` into shared `utils/service-line-infer.js` (used by both lead-webhook and call-attribution); call rows now populate `specific_service` + `service_bucket`, not just `service_line`, so `/admin/ads/service-lines` buckets phone leads the same as web leads. (3) Bridge backfill now resolves the lead via `findLeadForCall` when `call_log.lead_id` is null (lead matched by phone/customer in metadata, not by the `twilio_call_sid` join) instead of dropping it. (4) `partial_success` is now terminal in `priorUploadSkipReason` — a PARTIAL_SUCCESS request returns only aggregate counts, so re-uploading the whole batch would duplicate the already-accepted records; it's surfaced via `error_message` for manual review instead.
## 2026-06-26 — Customer Health: consolidate three colliding scorers into one engine (feat/customer-health-consolidation)

**Context.** `/admin/health` was driven by THREE nightly jobs colliding on `customer_health_scores`: (1) `customer-health-v2.js` @ 2:00AM wrote `customers.health_score`/`health_risk` — read by nothing (dead compute); (2) `customer-health.js` @ 2:15AM wrote the full diagnostic row (6 sub-scores + overall/grade/churn) with **Algorithm A** (weighted avg of sub-scores), vocab `low/moderate/high/critical`; (3) `customer-intelligence/health-scorer.js` @ 3:00AM **overwrote** overall/grade/churn on the same row with **Algorithm B** (signal-weighted), vocab `healthy/watch/at_risk/critical`, leaving A's sub-scores intact. Net: every row ended the night a hybrid (radar = A, headline score = B), two engines with no shared math. This also caused a **live UI bug** — the dashboard's `RISK_LABELS`/`RISK_COLORS` only define `low/moderate/high/critical`, so after 3AM every non-`critical` customer rendered a blank/uncolored risk chip and the risk-breakdown donut bucketed them into nothing.

**Decision.** One engine. `customer-health.js` (Algorithm A) is now the **sole owner** of `overall_score`/`score_grade`/sub-scores/`churn_risk`/`churn_probability`/`churn_signals`/history/alerts. Its vocab (`low/moderate/high/critical`) is what the dashboard already renders, so making it canonical fixes the live chip/donut bug with **zero frontend change**. `health-scorer.js` is demoted to an **enrichment-only** layer that reads the canonical row and updates ONLY `upsell_opportunities`/`next_best_action`/`lifetime_value_estimate` (renamed `calculateAllHealthScores`→`enrichAllCustomers`, `calculateHealth`→`enrichCustomer`; `identifyUpsells` unchanged; `determineNextAction` re-mapped to A's vocab). The 2:00AM (v2) and 2:15AM (standalone A) crons are removed; scoring now runs once nightly inside the 3AM Customer Intelligence Pipeline: **detect signals → score (A) → enrich (B) → outreach**.

**Signal-fold (the one behavior change).** To avoid regressing signal-driven churn detection when B stops scoring, A now reads `customer_signals` and folds them into the canonical score: `summarizeBehavioralSignals` (pure, exported, tested) returns a **bounded** net adjustment (`SIGNAL_SCORE_FLOOR -20`..`SIGNAL_SCORE_CEIL +10`, so the 6-factor diagnostic stays dominant and the radar never diverges from the headline by more than the cap) plus the negative drivers normalized into `churn_signals` (`warning`→`moderate`, `critical` stays `critical`, `info` never a driver). Because a `critical`-severity behavioral signal lands in `churn_signals`, `determineChurnRisk` escalates to `critical` automatically — so a signal-only churner (clean billing but "switching to Orkin") is now caught. Signal detection runs **before** scoring in the pipeline so the folded signals are tonight's.

**Other touch points.** Scheduler retention query: `whereIn('churn_risk', ['at_risk','critical'])`→`['high','critical']`, and `where('scored_at', today)`→`whereRaw('scored_at::date = ?', [today])` because A writes `scored_at` as a timestamp (B wrote a date string). `admin-customer-intel.js /scan` now mirrors the pipeline (detect→score→enrich). `admin-health.js` dashboard at-risk band → `['high','critical']`, stale dual-vocab comment refreshed. `retention-agent-tools.js run_overall_scores` updated to the score+enrich flow with the correct require path (the prior `require('./health-scorer')` was a pre-existing broken path; the other broken paths in that file — `detect_signals`/`get_retention_metrics`/`generate_retention_outreach` → `signal-detector`/`retention-engine` — are left for a separate fix, out of scope). New migration `20260626000009_drop_dead_customer_health_columns.js` drops the unread `customers.health_score`/`health_risk` (reverse of `…063`, guarded). `customer-health-v2.js` deleted (explicitly approved).

**Verification.** Rewrote `customer-intelligence-health-scorer.test.js` to assert enrichment writes ONLY the 3 intelligence columns (never score/risk/sub-scores), skips the write when no canonical row exists, and maps `determineNextAction` to the new vocab. New `customer-health-signal-fold.test.js` covers the bounded adjustment + driver normalization. 12 tests green; 24 across all touched suites; all changed files `node --check`-clean; real require path (`customer-health → signal-detector`, acyclic) confirmed. **OWNER after deploy:** migration runs on deploy; after one nightly cycle verify `SELECT churn_risk, count(*) FROM customer_health_scores GROUP BY 1` shows only `low/moderate/high/critical`, `customers.health_score`/`health_risk` are gone, dashboard risk chips are colored/labeled, and radar sub-score avg ≈ headline (within the signal cap). Follow-up PR 2 (separate): event-driven rescoring on hot signals + proactive touch for healthy-but-quiet customers.

## 2026-06-26 — Customer Health: event-driven rescoring on hot inbound signals (feat/customer-health-event-rescore)

**Context.** PR 2a, on top of the consolidated single engine. The nightly Customer Intelligence Pipeline scores everyone once at 3 AM ET, so a hot inbound signal — a customer texting about a competitor, a cancellation, or a price complaint — could sit up to ~24h before it moved the score and the owner heard about it. Existing webhook rescore triggers (Stripe payment-failure/refund, review submit) already call `scoreCustomer` on the relevant event, but **inbound SMS — the highest-value real-time churn signal — was the gap**: nothing detected signals or rescored on an inbound text, and the owner churn-alert only fired inside the nightly retention pipeline.

**Change.** New `server/services/customer-intelligence/event-rescore.js` exporting `rescoreOnInboundMessage(customerId, {source})`: reads the customer's prior `churn_risk`, runs the existing per-customer `SignalDetector.detectSignals(customerId)` (keyword + AI-sentiment on recent inbound SMS) so the rescore reflects the new message, rescores via the canonical `customer-health.scoreCustomer` (which folds the fresh signals), and alerts the owner **only on a transition INTO critical**. Wired into `twilio-webhook.js` right after the inbound `sms_log` insert (`messageType === 'inbound' && customer?.id`), fire-and-forget so it never delays the webhook ack — mirroring the adjacent `estimate-conversion-agent.processInboundSms` call.

**Alert + dedup.** `sendCriticalChurnAlert` sends Adam an internal-alert SMS (`TwilioService.sendSMS(ADAM_PHONE, …, { messageType: 'internal_alert' })`, the canonical internal-alert path) marked "(live)", with the top churn driver and the customer's phone — an immediate heads-up, distinct from the nightly retention alert which carries the outreach draft. Dedup is the **transition guard**: fire only when `churnRisk === 'critical' && priorRisk !== 'critical'`, so it fires once at the crossing, never on every subsequent message while already critical. The nightly pipeline uses `scoreAllCustomers` (not this path), so it can't double-fire the live alert.

**Gating + safety.** Entire feature behind `GATE_EVENT_RESCORE` (fail-closed, `=== 'true'`): when off it is a complete no-op and behavior is exactly the nightly-only path. `rescoreOnInboundMessage` never throws (internal try/catch) since it's called fire-and-forget; silent when `ADAM_PHONE` is unset. Reuses existing dedup downstream — `detectSignals` dedupes against unresolved `customer_signals`, `scoreCustomer`→`health-alerts` dedupes the `critical_risk` alert row.

**Verification.** New `event-rescore.test.js` (6): gate-off no-op; detect-before-score ordering; alert on transition into critical (asserts recipient/body/`internal_alert` opts); no re-alert when already critical; no alert when not critical; critical transition with no `ADAM_PHONE` → no alert, no throw. All 20 blast-radius suites green (event-rescore + twilio-webhook + the health suites); changed files `node --check`-clean; module require path (`event-rescore → customer-health/signal-detector/twilio`) confirmed acyclic. The full-suite pre-existing failures (`admin-customers.js:1038` require-cycle, DB-connection infra) are unrelated and present on `main`. **OWNER:** flip `GATE_EVENT_RESCORE=true` on Railway (and confirm `ADAM_PHONE` is set) to enable; leave off to keep nightly-only. Remaining PR-2 work (separate): proactive touch for healthy-but-quiet customers; optionally route the existing Stripe payment-failure rescore through `rescoreOnInboundMessage`'s transition-alert too.

**Codex round 1 (1 P2, addressed).** **Make the critical-transition alert dedupe atomic.** The original `priorRisk !== 'critical'` guard was check-then-act: two concurrent inbound texts for the same customer could both read the pre-critical row and both alert. Replaced with the codebase's atomic-claim idiom (cf. `arrival_sms_sent_at`): new nullable `customer_health_scores.critical_alert_sent_at` (migration `…0010` + scorer auto-heal), and the alert now fires only when `claimCriticalAlert()` wins a conditional `UPDATE … SET critical_alert_sent_at = now() WHERE churn_risk = 'critical' AND critical_alert_sent_at IS NULL` (Postgres row-locks the single current row → exactly one concurrent caller gets rowcount 1). The canonical scorer (`customer-health.js`) clears the column whenever the customer is not critical, so a later re-entry re-claims and re-alerts — one live alert per critical episode. `priorRisk` read removed (the claim is the dedupe). Tests updated to model claim-won (rowcount 1 → alert) vs claim-lost (0 → no alert); 18 health-suite tests green.

**Codex round 2 (3 P2, all addressed).**
- **Preserve the critical-transition guard.** Round 1's claim-only check treated any not-yet-claimed critical row as a fresh crossing, so a customer already critical (via nightly/Stripe scoring, which don't run this path, or before the gate was enabled) would falsely alert "just dropped to CRITICAL" on their next text. Restored the `priorRisk !== 'critical'` read **alongside** the atomic claim: priorRisk gives the episode-level transition semantics (suppresses already-critical), the claim gives concurrency safety (one winner among simultaneous crossings). Both are needed; neither alone is correct.
- **Rescore handled inbound SMS branches too.** The hook only fired on the fall-through `messageType === 'inbound'` path, but an exact "CANCEL"/STOP is classified as `opt_out` and returns earlier — so the strongest churn signal still waited for nightly. Extracted a local `fireEventRescore(source)` helper (gated, fire-and-forget) and now call it on the **opt-out/cancel branch** (`source: 'sms_opt_out'`, before its early return) as well as the general inbound path. The owner alert is internal, unaffected by the customer's SMS opt-out.
- **Make signal detection safe for concurrent inbound texts.** `signal-detector.detectSignals` was read-unresolved-then-insert with no atomic guard, so two concurrent inbound webhooks for one customer could double-insert a signal type and double-count its folded weight. New migration `…0011` adds a **partial unique index** `customer_signals_unresolved_uniq (customer_id, signal_type) WHERE resolved = false` (dedups any existing unresolved duplicates first), and the insert now swallows `23505` — the losing race is ignored. A resolved signal can still be re-detected later. 21 health-suite tests green.

**Codex round 3 (3 P2, all addressed).**
- **Record an opt-out signal before rescoring.** The opt-out hook only re-ran `detectSignals`, whose keyword rule fires `DOWNGRADE_REQUEST` for `cancel`/`stop service`/`not renew` — so a bare `STOP`/`UNSUBSCRIBE`/`QUIT` produced no signal and the rescore was a no-op. `signal-detector` now also keys on `message_type === 'opt_out'` in the recent-inbound scan (the opt-out branch logs the row before firing the rescore), raising the same `DOWNGRADE_REQUEST` regardless of the exact keyword. Kept in signal-detector (not the webhook) so it benefits the nightly batch too; consistent with the existing "cancellation language → DOWNGRADE_REQUEST" rule (no new business judgment).
- **Rescore matched customers on tracking numbers.** The general-path hook was gated on `messageType === 'inbound'`, but an existing customer texting a churn message to a domain/van tracking number is logged as `*_lead`. Dropped the gate — `fireEventRescore('inbound_sms')` runs for any matched customer (it already no-ops without `customer?.id`, and non-customer leads return earlier).
- **Deduplicate health alerts during concurrent live rescores.** `health-alerts.generateAlerts` deduped with SELECT-then-INSERT, so two concurrent rescores could both create an active `critical_risk` row (the SMS was already atomically deduped, but the admin inbox wasn't). New migration `…0012` adds a partial unique index `customer_health_alerts_active_uniq (customer_id, alert_type) WHERE status IN ('new','acknowledged')` (demotes existing active duplicates to `dismissed` first), and the insert swallows `23505`. 21 health-suite tests green; all changed files `node --check`-clean. (`signal-detector` has no unit harness; the opt-out rule is a 2-line extension of the existing untested keyword rules.)

**Codex round 4 (2 P2, all addressed).**
- **Restrict active-alert uniqueness to rule alerts.** Round 3's index was table-wide, but 11 other paths (`stripe.js`, `billing-cron` ×7, `stripe-webhook`) insert one-off operational alerts that legitimately repeat an `alert_type` per customer (one per incident, keyed in `trigger_data`) — the broad index would 23505 their second incident and drop it. Migration `…0012` rewritten: both the dedup-demote and the index are now scoped to the seven `generateAlerts` RULE types (`score_drop`/`critical_risk`/`service_gap`/`payment_issue`/`low_engagement`/`satisfaction_drop`/`new_customer_risk`); index renamed `customer_health_alerts_active_rule_uniq`. Operational alerts are untouched.
- **Avoid claiming the live alert before delivery is possible.** The claim was taken before the deliverability check, so with the gate on but `ADAM_PHONE` unset (or a Twilio failure) the claim was burned with nothing delivered — that episode would never retry until the customer recovered and re-entered critical. Now: `ADAM_PHONE` is checked **before** claiming (no recipient → no claim), `sendCriticalChurnAlert` returns a delivered boolean (false on throw or `sent === false`), and on a failed send the claim is **released** (`releaseCriticalAlert` sets `critical_alert_sent_at = null`) so the next inbound text retries. New test covers the release-on-failure path. 22 health-suite tests green.

**Codex round 5 (3 P2, all addressed).**
- **Handle failed alert redirects as undelivered.** `internal_alert` sends to owner numbers are redirected to Waves notifications, which return `success: true` with `notificationUndelivered`/`notificationError` (no `sent` field) on failure — so the `sent === false` check treated them as delivered and burned the claim. Added `isAlertDelivered(r)` treating any failure shape (`success === false`, `sent === false`, `blocked`, `notificationUndelivered`, `notificationError`) as undelivered; new test covers the redirect-undelivered case.
- **Distinguish wrong-number opt-outs from churn intent.** A "wrong number" report is also logged as `message_type: 'opt_out'` (with `opt_out_reason: 'wrong_number'` in metadata). The opt-out detector now parses `metadata.opt_out_reason` and excludes `wrong_number`, so a recycled/wrong number isn't scored as cancellation intent.
- **Ensure the claim column independently.** The `critical_alert_sent_at` auto-heal was nested under the `!hasPmtScore` branch, so a table auto-created with `payment_score` but without the claim column would never get it (and `claimCriticalAlert` would hit an undefined column). Moved the column-ensure out of that branch to run regardless. 23 health-suite tests green; all changed files `node --check`-clean.

## 2026-06-26 — Meta (Facebook/Instagram) Ads lane: ingestion + attribution + CAPI (feat/meta-ads-lane)

**Context.** Second ad channel into the PPC section, after the Google Ads close-the-loop work. Research confirmed the foundation was ready: `ad_campaigns.platform` is an unconstrained string already listing `facebook`; the PPC dashboard + `admin-ads` read paths are platform-agnostic (no `platform='google_ads'` filter), so Meta rows surface automatically once synced. Everything Meta-Ads was net-new (existing Facebook code is organic Pages posting only). Ships dark behind creds/gates (owner provisions Meta Marketing API + CAPI credentials).

**Phase 1 — ingestion.** New `services/ads/meta-ads.js` mirrors `google-ads.js`: `syncCampaigns` + `syncDailyPerformance` pull `/act_<id>/campaigns` + `/insights` (Graph Marketing API, `fetch` + cursor pagination) into the SAME `ad_campaigns`/`ad_performance_daily` tables with `platform='facebook'` (no schema change). Pure mappers (`mapStatus`/`mapCampaign`/`mapInsightRow`/`sumActions`) for testability; Meta-only fields fit `metadata`. Daily 6:15am ET scheduler cron (no-op unless `META_ADS_*` set) + `POST /api/admin/ads/sync/meta`. Remote budget/pause stays Google-only (Meta read-only for now). `META_ADS_ACCESS_TOKEN` (ads_read system user) + `META_ADS_ACCOUNT_ID` documented.

**Phase 2 — attribution.** New migration `20260626000014` adds `fbclid`/`fbc`/`fbp` to `leads` + `ad_service_attribution` (mirrors the gbraid/wbraid migration). `lead-webhook.js` parses + stores them (mirror of the gclid path), and `determineLeadSource` now resolves an fbclid-bearing lead with no clearer source to **paid `facebook`** (Meta auto-appends fbclid even without UTMs; explicit `utm_source=facebook` still wins). The astro-side capture (`wavespestcontrol-astro/src/lib/attribution.ts` — fbclid from URL + `_fbc`/`_fbp` cookies) is a **separate repo/PR**; until it deploys, fbclid still arrives via query/body params.

**Phase 3 — CAPI close-the-loop.** New `services/ads/meta-data-manager.js` = the Meta analog of `data-manager.js`, uploading qualified leads (`Lead`) + completed-job revenue (`Purchase`) to the Conversions API. **Reuses** data-manager's candidate collectors (extended additively to also carry `fbclid`/`fbc`/`fbp` — the Google path ignores them) + its hashing helpers, so both channels pull the SAME rows. Match keys: `fbc`/`fbp` (or `fbc` rebuilt from `fbclid`) + SHA-256 hashed email/phone. Safety mirrors Google: real sends require `META_CAPI_ALLOW_UPLOADS=true`; otherwise events route to Meta **Test Events** via `META_CAPI_TEST_EVENT_CODE` (not counted), and it refuses to send if neither is set. De-duped per `event_id` via new `meta_conversion_uploads` log (migration `20260626000015`); per-type advisory lock; daily 6:45am ET opt-in cron (`META_CAPI_CRON_ENABLED`); `GET/POST /api/admin/analytics/meta-capi/{readiness,upload}` (upload defaults to a dry run).

**Verification.** New suites `meta-ads-sync` (10) + `lead-webhook-meta-attribution` (7) + `meta-capi` (9); existing `data-manager` (still green — collector changes are additive). All changed files `node --check`-clean. Ships entirely dark: no `META_ADS_*`/`META_CAPI_*` env → every new path no-ops. **Owner to go live:** provision Marketing API token + ad account id (Phase 1), then Pixel/dataset id + CAPI token + `META_CAPI_ALLOW_UPLOADS`/`_CRON_ENABLED` (Phase 3); merge the astro fbclid-capture PR (Phase 2).

**Codex round 1 (Meta lane; 2×P1 + 2×P2, all addressed).** (P1) Meta CAPI rejects the entire batch on any event >7 days old — added an `event_too_old` skip guard (hard-capped 7d) and tightened the CAPI collection/cron/admin window 90→7 days so old events never enter a batch. (P1) Default Marketing/Graph API version `v21.0` is expired — bumped to `v23.0` and documented that Meta deprecates versions ~yearly (the `META_ADS_API_VERSION` override is authoritative). (P2) `BudgetManager.adjustBudgets` selected ALL active campaigns and would throttle Meta budgets it can't remotely control — scoped it to `platform='google_ads'`. (P2) CAPI upload-log write failures were swallowed as warnings while the row was reported sent (defeating dedupe) — now use `Promise.allSettled`, log an ERROR with the failure count, and surface `logFailures` in the result (Meta's event_id 48h dedup is the short-term backstop). Tests: `meta-capi` now 10; 41 across Meta+data-manager suites green.

**Codex round 2 (Meta lane; 3×P2, all addressed).** (1) `admin-ads` pause/enable/budget handlers called the Google API + flipped local status for ANY campaign — now reject non-`google_ads` campaigns with a 400 ("manage in Ads Manager") BEFORE any local mutation, so a Meta row can't drift. (2) The quote-wizard capture path (QuotePage.jsx + public-quote.js + public-property-lookup.js) stored only gclid/wbraid/gbraid — added fbclid/`_fbc`/`_fbp` capture+storage (mirror of the gclid path) so Meta leads via the estimator carry the click ids for attribution + CAPI. (3) `determineLeadSource` now also takes `_fbc` (the cookie form of the Meta click id) in its fallback paid-Facebook rule — an fbc-only lead (URL fbclid lost after navigation) is classified paid Meta, not organic; `_fbp` alone is still excluded (ambient). Tests: +`_fbc`-only source case; 42 across Meta+data-manager suites green.

**Codex round 3 (Meta lane; 3×P2, all addressed).** (1) Quote-wizard leads from a Meta ad (fbclid/_fbc, no FB UTM) were still resolved to Main Site because `resolveLeadSource` ignored Meta signals — added a Meta branch (fbclid/_fbc/utm_source=facebook → 'Facebook', FK via a `LIKE '%facebook%'` lookup, never Main Site), mirroring the webhook's determineLeadSource. (2) The read-only platform guard was missing on `POST /campaigns/:id/mode` (which rewrites budget_mode + daily_budget_current locally, reachable from advisor-apply) — added it, so Meta campaigns can't be driven to spent/stop locally. (3) Meta `syncCampaigns`/`syncDailyPerformance` did select-then-insert with no unique (platform, platform_campaign_id) — wrapped both in `runExclusive` (per-edge advisory lock) so overlapping cron instances / the admin /sync/meta can't double-insert a campaign. Tests still green (46 across the ads suites).

**Codex round 4 (Meta lane; 3×P2, all addressed).** (1) `/advisor/apply` calls BudgetManager.setBudget/setMode directly (bypassing the per-endpoint guards), so a Meta recommendation could still mutate local budget — moved the `platform==='google_ads'` guard INTO `setBudget`/`setMode` themselves (throws for non-Google), covering every caller. (2) QuotePage's attribution presence-check dropped the whole object when only `_fbp` was present — added `!fbp` so the CAPI match key is preserved (view-through/direct-return scenario); `_fbp` still isn't a *source* signal, only a match key. (3) `logUpload` unconditionally merged, so a forced validate-only/test run could overwrite an already-`sent` row with `validated`/`sent_at=null` and make the next live cron re-upload — now it skips the write when a prior `sent` row exists (never downgrades a real send). Tests: +downgrade-protection (meta-capi 11); 43 across the Meta suites green.

## 2026-06-26 — Customer Health: "Quiet" surface — proactive reach-out list (feat/customer-health-quiet-surface)

**Context.** PR 2b, the last of the customer-health lane. The at-risk views only surface customers whose score is bad (`high`/`critical` churn risk). But the common way customers churn isn't a dramatic signal — it's quietly feeling forgotten ("the company stopped caring"). A customer with a perfectly healthy score who simply hasn't had a visit or a reply in months is invisible to the at-risk system. This adds a read-only surface for exactly those people so the owner can make a proactive personal check-in. Deliberately **surface-only — no automated messages** (owner choice: for a one-tech op, a "who to call" list beats auto-texting happy customers and the brand risk that carries).

**Backend.** New `GET /api/admin/health/quiet` on `admin-health.js` (inherits the router-wide `adminAuthenticate`). Finds active real customers (`pipeline_stage IN active_customer/won/at_risk`) in the **healthy band** (`churn_risk IN ('low','moderate')` — i.e. NOT already in the at-risk views) whose **last meaningful touch** is older than `HEALTH_QUIET_DAYS` (default 45, env-tunable, floored at 7). "Meaningful touch" = most recent COMPLETED service OR INBOUND SMS — automated outbound (reminders/receipts) deliberately doesn't count, since it doesn't make a customer feel cared for. Brand-new customers awaiting a first visit are excluded (`COALESCE(member_since, created_at) < cutoff`). The whole query is wrapped in try/catch → degrades to an empty list, never crashes the route. The non-SQL logic lives in a tiny testable helper `services/customer-intelligence/quiet-customers.js` (`LAST_TOUCH_SQL`, `resolveQuietDays`, `mapQuietRow` — `days_since_touch` is null for a never-touched customer, who floors to epoch and sorts first).

**Frontend.** New "Quiet" tab in `CustomerHealthTabs.jsx` → `CustomerHealthSection` (between Health Scores and Alerts), matching the existing inline `COLORS`/`Card`/`Badge`/`mono` style. A one-line explainer card + a table (Customer / Tier / City / Score / Last touch / Phone) sorted by longest silence first; empty state when everyone healthy has been touched recently. Self-contained `QuietTab` component, its own `adminFetch('/admin/health/quiet')`, no new deps. (NB: `/admin/health` redirects to `/admin/customers?view=health`, which renders `CustomerHealthSection` from `CustomerHealthTabs.jsx` — NOT the legacy unmounted `CustomerHealthPage.jsx`.)

**Verification.** New `quiet-customers.test.js` (7) covers `resolveQuietDays` (default/override/floor/invalid) and `mapQuietRow` (days computation, never-touched → null, monthly_rate parse). Changed backend files `node --check`-clean; `CustomerHealthPage.jsx` parses clean via esbuild. **UI not yet rendered in a real browser** — recommend a quick visual check of the Quiet tab before relying on it. **OWNER:** optionally set `HEALTH_QUIET_DAYS` (default 45); no gate — read-only surface, safe to ship live. This completes the customer-health lane (engine consolidation #2121 → event-driven rescore #2128 → quiet surface).

**Codex round 1 (2 P2, all addressed).**
- **Add the Quiet tab to the MOUNTED health view.** The tab was first added to `CustomerHealthPage.jsx`, but `/admin/health` redirects to `/admin/customers?view=health`, which renders `CustomerHealthSection` from `CustomerHealthTabs.jsx` — so the page I edited is never mounted. Reverted `CustomerHealthPage.jsx` to `origin/main` and added `QuietTab` + the tab wiring to `CustomerHealthTabs.jsx`/`CustomerHealthSection` (the live component) instead.
- **Exclude archived customers from the quiet list.** Archiving sets `customers.deleted_at` without clearing `active` or the pipeline stage, so the query (which only checked `active` + `pipeline_stage`) could surface deleted customers' names/phones for outreach. Added `whereNull('c.deleted_at')` alongside the existing filters (matching the canonical live-customer predicate). 7 helper tests still green; live JSX esbuild-clean.

**Context.** Cleanup tail from the customer-health lane. `retention-agent-tools.js` (the Customer Retention managed-agent tool executor) `require`d four of its dependencies as `./signal-detector` / `./retention-engine` / `./health-scorer` — but those modules live in `server/services/customer-intelligence/`, not `server/services/`. So `detect_signals`, `get_retention_metrics`, `generate_retention_outreach`, and `identify_upsells` threw `MODULE_NOT_FOUND` whenever the agent invoked them. Pre-existing (predates the lane); PR #2121 fixed only the one path it touched (`run_overall_scores`) and explicitly deferred the rest.

## 2026-06-26 — Event-driven churn alert: admin notification instead of owner SMS (feat/churn-alert-as-notification)

**Context.** The event-driven rescore (#2128) fired its live critical-churn heads-up via `TwilioService.sendSMS(ADAM_PHONE, …, { messageType: 'internal_alert' })`. In practice that already *redirected* to the admin notification bell+push (owner-phone + `internal_alert` type → `redirectInternalAdminSmsToNotification` → `triggerNotification('internal_admin_alert', …)`, SMS suppressed), but it relied on the owner-phone heuristic and read as "send an SMS." Owner asked to make it an explicit admin notification.

**Change.** `event-rescore.js` `sendCriticalChurnAlert` now calls `triggerNotification('internal_admin_alert', { title, body, link: '/admin/customers?view=health' })` directly — bell + push to active admins, respecting per-admin notification prefs; no SMS, no `ADAM_PHONE` dependency, and (as always for this concept) **never any message to the customer**. Delivered = `stats.bellWritten || stats.push.sent > 0`; on an undelivered/errored notification the atomic claim is released so a later text retries (unchanged dedup semantics). Dropped the pre-claim `ADAM_PHONE` gate (notifications go to admins, not a phone) and the SMS-shape `isAlertDelivered` helper.

**Verification.** `event-rescore.test.js` reworked to mock `triggerNotification` (9 tests): gate-off no-op; detect-before-score; posts `internal_admin_alert` with the right title/body/link on a won claim; no claim/alert when already-critical / lost-claim / not-critical; releases the claim on a thrown or undelivered notification; counts push-only as delivered. `node --check`-clean; require path (`event-rescore → notification-triggers`) resolves. No SMS path remains in the module.

**Change.** Repointed all four requires to `./customer-intelligence/...`. The target modules exist and export the called methods (`SignalDetector.detectAllSignals`, `RetentionEngine.getMetrics` / `generateRetentionOutreach`, `HealthScorer.identifyUpsells` — all singletons). No behavior change beyond the tools now loading. Verified: no `require('./signal-detector'|'./retention-engine'|'./health-scorer')` remain in `server/services/*.js`; `node --check`-clean; all four tool require paths resolve at runtime. Closes the cleanup deferred in the #2121/#2128 entries; the customer-health lane is now fully closed.

## 2026-07-04 — Dashboard mobile scorecard: honest LTV:CAC, CAC payback, adjusted-EBITDA bridge, per-card verdicts (feat/mobile-scorecard-dashboard)

**Context.** Owner asked for a ServiceTitan-class mobile scorecard pass on `/admin/dashboard` with hard metric-correctness rules: LTV:CAC must be gross-profit-based (never revenue), CAC must be all-in (sales + marketing, or clearly labeled otherwise), small-sample warnings must be visible without a tooltip, EBITDA must be a separate adjusted-EBITDA bridge never mixed with gross margin, and every major card must answer "What happened?" / "What should I do?".

**Where the formulas live (dev notes).**
- **LTV:CAC + bands + CAC payback** — `server/services/capital-allocation.js` (pure). Numerator: 12-mo gross-profit LTV from `server/services/channel-attribution.js` (`projectedLtv12moGP` for recurring + realized GP); denominator: all-in marketing cost (platform ad spend + `channel_fixed_costs` retainers + referral rewards) — there is no separate sales payroll to include (owner sells); if one ever exists it belongs in the denominator. `paybackMonths = 12 ÷ exact ratio` (the LTV is a 12-month figure). Headline adds blended CAC + payback.
- **Adjusted-EBITDA bridge** — `server/services/ebitda-bridge.js` (pure) + `GET /admin/dashboard/ebitda-bridge` (admin-dashboard.js, wave4 of `loadAll`). Revenue − COGS (job-costing-burdened) = GP; − marketing actuals = contribution; − owner-entered `company_financials` overhead (vehicle/insurance/software/admin·customers/12, prorated by elapsed month fraction) = adjusted EBITDA. Stops at Contribution when overhead is unentered; materially uncosted revenue (>5%) surfaces as a visible caveat. "Adjusted": before owner comp, interest, taxes, D&A.
- **Verdicts + sample tiers** — `client/src/pages/admin/dashboard/scorecard-metrics.js` (pure, vitest-covered): `confidenceTier` (n<5 ⇒ visible amber pill, never tooltip), per-card verdict builders (capital, EBITDA, capture, funnel, completion, MRR, aging). Small samples force a neutral "too few to judge" action.

**UI.** `Verdict.jsx` (what-happened → do-next footer on every major card), `SampleBadge.jsx`/`LowSamplePill` (visible warnings), `EbitdaBridgeCard.jsx` (waterfall, own card BESIDE gross margin in Profit), `FormulaNote.jsx` (collapsible formula footnotes). `CapitalAllocationCard` moved CAC/payback/spend/customers out of the row tooltip onto the rows and corrected its footer label (was "gross profit ÷ ad spend" — undersold the all-in denominator). Mobile (<md): the five sections render one at a time behind the jump-nav pills (real tabs, controlled `DashboardJumpNav`), the 9-pill period strip becomes a native select with readable labels, each section header carries a "What is this?" explainer dropdown, and the sticky bar offset was fixed to sit flush under the fixed header (was `top:52px` inside a scroll container whose paddingTop already includes the header ⇒ see-through band; now `top:-16px`). Desktop scroll+observer behavior unchanged.

**Verification.** 329/329 client vitest (23 scorecard-metrics + 5 mobile-tab/select/explainer + EBITDA fixtures in the page test), server jest: 8 ebitda-bridge + 4 payback additions (capital-allocation suite now 19), `check:portal-brand` clean, vite build clean; live 390×844 pass via Chrome DevTools against seeded local dev data (blended 6.2:1 headline, low-sample Facebook pill, full bridge $2,790→$1,243 with prorated marketing/overhead).

## 2026-07-04 — Growth Command Center Phase 4: net-MRR bridge (feat/dashboard-mrr-bridge)

**Context.** Phase 4 of the owner-approved 7-phase dashboard lane (phases 1–3 merged 07-02/03; the scorecard PR #2335 delivered Phase 6's CAC payback + Phase 5's profit-bridge core out of order). The Retention section showed THAT recurring revenue moved (Net MRR tile, 12-mo trend) but not WHY.

**Change.** New pure `server/services/mrr-bridge.js` (`buildBridgeMonths` core + `computeMrrBridge` DB wrapper) + `GET /admin/dashboard/mrr-bridge?months=6` (clamped 2–12, dashboardCache, wave5 of `loadAll`). Exact months diff consecutive `customer_mrr_snapshots` months: entrant converted in-month (CONVERSION_DATE_SQL) ⇒ new, else reactivated; departed ⇒ churned at prior rate; rate deltas ⇒ expansion/contraction — every customer in exactly one bucket, so start + Σ = end to the cent. Months without both snapshots DEGRADE (never hide): customers-table approximation (cohort's exit convention — churned_at, else stage-change month for churned/dormant, else deleted_at) at current rates, `degraded: true`. In-progress current month flagged (daily upsert until month-end freeze). Client `MrrBridgeCard` (div-bar waterfall idiom, month strip w/ dashed degraded pills, in-progress chip, `mrrBridgeVerdict` what-happened/do-next, FormulaNote) beside MRR Trend in Retention (2-col desktop, own MobileFold on phone).

**Verification.** `mrr-bridge.test.js` 10 tests (new-vs-reactivated split, expansion/contraction + to-the-cent additivity, month chaining, degraded fallback incl. boundary month whose predecessor lacks snapshots, ET date normalization via local getters — node-pg DATE cells); `mrrBridgeVerdict` 5 tests; page-test fixtures; client 335/335; raw SQL (to_char conversion/exit months) validated read-only against prod; live 390px pass with seeded two-month snapshots (bridge $344→$365 additive, degraded month dashed w/ approximate note; QA rows deleted after). Prod reality: snapshots exist for 2026-06 + 2026-07, so July is the first exact month (its −$55 net reconciles with the Net MRR tile) and fidelity grows monthly.

## 2026-07-04 — Growth Command Center Phase 5: Operating Costs + profit-bridge basis + margin by line (feat/dashboard-profit-bridge)

**Context.** Phase 5 remainder after the scorecard PR (#2335) shipped the EBITDA bridge running on pricing-column approximations. Three gaps: no owner-editable operating costs (the ovh_* block the plan specified), the revenue-settings PUT silently reset every unlisted company_financials column to defaults on any save (fresh 4-field insert; zero client consumers so latent), and the blended gross margin hid which LINES carry or drag it.

**Change.**
- Migration `20260704120000`: nullable `ovh_office_payroll/rent/insurance/software/vehicle_fixed/other_ga` + `overhead_entered_at` on company_financials — deliberately NEW columns; the existing per-month cost columns are PRICING inputs and overloading them risks double-count/rewrite in both directions. No seeds: unentered keeps the pricing-defaults fallback.
- `PUT /api/admin/revenue/settings` rebuilt around pure `buildSettingsRow` (exported): reads the latest row, carries every prior value forward, overlays only explicitly-sent camelCase fields, validates ≥0 (null clears an ovh figure), stamps `overhead_entered_at` on any overhead touch; same-day saves update in place instead of stacking duplicate effective_dates. Regression: `admin-revenue-settings-merge.test.js` (5).
- `services/ebitda-bridge.js` generalized: overhead = `{ basis: 'entered'|'pricing_defaults', components, enteredAt }` (legacy shape still accepted as pricing_defaults — all 8 prior tests untouched). Basis semantics: 'entered' figures are deliberate so the waterfall ALWAYS completes (even $0); approximations complete only when > 0. NEW `cogsSplit` (labor/products/drive+equipment actuals from job_costs, completed-gated via scheduled_services) renders as indented COGS detail reconciling to the headline via an "Unsplit" line. Card states the basis ON the card (amber note pointing at Settings → Financials → Operating Costs when approximated; entered stamp otherwise); `ebitdaVerdict` carries the same caveat. +7 bridge tests (15).
- Settings → Financials → **Operating Costs** leaf (`OperatingCostsSettingsTab`): 6 currency inputs with plain-language hints (payroll ≠ tech labor; vehicle fixed ≠ fuel), monthly total, last-entered stamp, fail-closed load, dirty-only PUT.
- **Margin by Service Line** card in Profit (`MarginByLineBars`): reuses `GET /admin/revenue/overview` `byServiceLine` (zero new SQL; wave6 of `loadAll`), horizontal bars vs the owner's `gross_margin` kpi-target tick, <45% floor red, n<5 lines get visible Low-sample pills and neutral tone. `classifyServiceLine` extracted to `services/service-line.js` — the intelligence-bar copy had drifted (missing One-Time branch, so one-time services misfiled as Pest Control in IB answers); both call sites now share one classifier (turf regression suite still green).

**Verification.** Client 335/335, server 55 across touched suites, brand clean, build clean. job_costs split SQL validated read-only against prod ($168.58 labor / $36 drive, 6 completed MTD visits). ## 2026-07-04 — Growth Command Center Phase 6: lead funnel by source (feat/dashboard-lead-funnel)

## 2026-07-04 — Growth Command Center Phase 7: churn-reason taxonomy + Pareto (feat/churn-reason-taxonomy)

**Context.** Final phase of the 7-phase lane. Churn was a count and a dollar figure with no WHY — the legacy customers.churn_reason is a varchar(30) constant, and the customer's actual cancellation words lived only in service_requests.

**Change.**
- Migration `20260704180000`: `customers.churn_reason_code` varchar(40) + CHECK constraint (price / moving / service_quality / results / competitor / seasonal_pause / financial / no_longer_needed / other / unclassified — guarded, re-runnable), `churn_reason_detail` text (the customer's own words; legacy 30-char field kept + still written), `churn_mrr` decimal (rate snapshotted AT churn — monthly_rate gets zeroed later, which would rewrite the Pareto's dollars).
- `services/churn-classifier.js`: live GPT-5.5 via new `MODELS.ROUTES.churnClassify` → Claude FLAGSHIP fallback → **fail-closed 'unclassified'** on every miss (blank text, provider error, junk/unknown code, throw). Never hardcodes model ids.
- `cancellation-processor.js`: on first churn, synchronously stamps churn_mrr + detail + code='unclassified' INSIDE the existing billing wind-down; the AI classification runs as the LAST step of the request and its failure is logged but never enters `errors` — a model outage can neither block nor delay a cancellation nor flag the request for manual review. Already-churned customers keep their original taxonomy.
- `GET /admin/dashboard/churn-reasons?months=12` (clamped 3–24) + pure `services/churn-pareto.js`: grouped by COALESCE(code,'unclassified'), dollars = COALESCE(churn_mrr, monthly_rate, 0), internal names excluded; returns Pareto rows (desc lost MRR + cumulative %) with `unclassified` ALWAYS present and `unclassifiedShare` (customers basis) as the honesty metric.
- Client `ChurnParetoCard` in Retention ("Why Customers Leave", wave7 of loadAll): recharts ComposedChart (desc MRR bars + cumulative-% line), always-visible amber unclassified-share badge, `churnParetoVerdict` mapping the top classified reason to its lever (price → win/loss bands; service_quality → ops; seasonal → hold plan; ≥50% unclassified → "run the backfill before drawing conclusions"; small samples refuse reorganization advice), FormulaNote with the codes-from-Jul-2026 provenance.
- `scripts/backfill-churn-reason-codes.js` — **ships only; prod run stays owner-authorized**: DRY-RUN by default (--apply to write), idempotent (NULL/'unclassified' only), ' [ai-backfill]' provenance marker, INTERNAL_TEST_CUSTOMERS skipped, per-row fail-closed, boilerplate-constant text treated as no-text (no wasted model calls), source order: newest cancellation service_request description → churn_reason_detail → legacy churn_reason.

**Verification.** cancellation suite 18 (3 new: stamps + classified-code apply; classifier failure leaves unclassified with ok=true and empty errors; already-churned untouched + classifier not called), churn-classifier 6 (fail-closed contract + taxonomy lockstep with the migration), churn-pareto 3; client 343/343 (verdict tests + page fixtures incl. the always-visible unclassified badge); brand + build clean. Migration ran locally. Prod read-only: 1 churned account in the trailing 12 months ($55 — reconciles with the Net MRR tile) and 2 cancellation service_requests for the future backfill. Live 390px pass on 7 seeded churned rows ($604 Pareto, cumulative line, amber 14.3% badge, price-led verdict; rows deleted after); backfill dry-run smoke-tested on dev.

## 2026-07-04 — Estimate view: WaveGuard tier discounts visible again on bundle service cards (claude/waveguard-discounts-estimates-xdfh5x)

**Context.** Owner report (with a live screenshot): a pest + lawn (Silver) estimate on the React customer view showed "$130.50 /quarter" and "$74.70 /mo" with no sign the WaveGuard discount was applied. Root cause is **presentation, not math**: the server payload was correct (130.50 = 145 × 0.9; verified end-to-end by replaying generateEstimate → mapV1ToLegacyShape → buildPricingBundle), but the bundle layout had lost every discount cue. `showSavings={servicesLength === 1}` (from the "plan lines consolidated below the boxes" pass) suppressed the struck-through pre-discount anchor inside bundle cards, and the consolidated "You save … with WaveGuard {tier}" lines below the boxes only ever rendered for pest — `priceCardSavingsInfo` anchors on `frequency.perVisit`, which the server sets **only** on pest cadence rows. Non-pest bundle sections (own-cadence lawn ladders from `bundleSectionLadderForService`, mirrored tree/mosquito/termite rows) carry only `monthlyBase` (pre-discount monthly), so their savings line silently never appeared.

**Decision.** Client-only fix; the payload already carries everything needed:
- `PriceCard` gains `anchorPeriodPrice()`: anchor = `perVisit` when present (pest — per-visit equals per-interval), else `monthlyBase × intervalMonths`. Used by both the in-card math and the exported `priceCardSavingsInfo`, so the below-boxes bundle lines now render for every tier-discounted service, not just pest. The $0.05 rounding-noise floor (phantom-cent guard from #2319) is unchanged and applies to the fallback too.
- Bundle cards re-enable `showSavings` (gated on `section.waveGuardTierEligible !== false`) to restore the struck-through original price next to the member price — SSR-page parity. The in-card "You save" line stays bundle-suppressed (PriceCard still receives `waveGuardTier=null` in bundles), so the owner directive of ONE set of save lines below the boxes holds.
- Server contract pinned in `estimate-per-service-cadence.test.js`: `bundleSectionLadderForService` entries keep `monthlyBase` = pre-discount monthly. Dev-preview bundle fixture updated to the real payload shape (non-pest rows carry `monthlyBase`, never `perVisit`).

**Verification.** Client 340+5 new tests green (incl. monthlyBase-anchor and no-phantom-savings-on-Bronze cases); server per-service-cadence suite 17/17; Chrome-verified the preview bundle scenario at 1440 + 390: single "WaveGuard Gold" pill above the boxes, "~~$147/quarter~~ $124.95 /quarter" and "~~$100/mo~~ $85 /mo" anchors in-card, and all three "You save … with WaveGuard Gold" lines below the boxes; pest (Bronze) and accepted scenarios show no phantom anchors.

## 2026-07-04 — Lawn report rainfall: city-collective guard for single-cell model spikes (claude/irrigation-accuracy-check)

**Context.** The customer lawn report's "Rain in Your Area — Last 7 Days" chart is sourced from Open-Meteo `precipitation_sum` at the property's exact lat/lng. That value is a per-grid-cell MODELLED number, and on summer convective days a single cell can carry a spurious 3–8" bullseye its neighbours (and the real rain gauges) don't share. Owner-reported: a Nokomis property (John Ragsdale) showed **8.29" for one Wednesday** when the town gauges recorded ~0.25–0.76". Reproduced live: querying Open-Meteo across a ~3-mile box around Nokomis returned 0.06"–6.02" between adjacent cells for that same day — the property cell caught a model maximum the whole area didn't get. Not a unit bug (only one day inflated; the rain path already requests inches and never applies the mm factor) and not our arithmetic — the provider's single-cell value was wrong.

**Change (server, `application-conditions.js`).** `fetchServiceWeekWeather` now samples the customer's CITY (property cell + an 8-neighbour ring at ~0.045°, one multi-location Open-Meteo call) instead of one point. New pure, exported `resolveWeekRain(propSeries, cellSeriesList)`: if the property cell is a sharp outlier vs the city median on ANY day (`≥1.0"` absolute AND `≥2.5×` the day's median, with a 0.25" median floor), the whole week falls back to the city-collective (median) series and is flagged `rainConfidence:'low'`; otherwise the precise property series is kept unchanged (`property_point`, normal confidence). ET₀ stays the property-cell value (a smooth field, not spike-prone). Per-cell window validation preserves the prior "any missing day → untrusted → no chart" contract (incl. the `Number(null)===0` gap trap). Weekly total and daily chart always reconcile because both derive from the same resolved series.

**Change (plumbing + UI).** `report-data.js` carries `weekWeather.rainConfidence` → `buildLawnWaterContext` (`dailyRain7dConfidence`) → `reportV2.rain7dConfidence`. `RainLast7DaysChart` takes a `confidence` prop and, on `'low'`, renders the existing `ConfidenceTag` ("Limited data this week") below the bars — reusing the same muted-italic tag already on the Water card, no new styling. Owner decision (2026-07-04): badge ONLY on outlier weeks; normal weeks keep the precise per-address read with no badge. Scope: the rain card only — the Water This Week card's rain number self-corrects because the weekly total is replaced at the source; its confidence label was intentionally left to its existing advice-based logic.

**Verification.** New `rain-city-collective-fallback.test.js` (6): normal week untouched, the John/Nokomis 8.29" spike → city median + suspect, a genuinely wet week where neighbours AGREE is NOT flagged, sub-floor small day ignored, no-neighbours never fabricates a fallback. Full weather/report suites green (rainfall-7d-sum incl. the partial-window contract, irrigation-advice, irrigation-weekly-email, lawn-report-v2-consistency, weather-forecast, rain-out, pest-report-v2, completion-recap — 258 tests). Client build clean. Live 390px render of `/report-v2-preview` (Needs-attention tab) confirms the "Limited data this week" caption under the chart. No live DB in-session; the per-account geocode confirmation (John Ragsdale coords, Fern/Robert distance + service dates) was handed to the owner as a read-only SQL check.

## 2026-07-06 — Retire the pre-glass theme: liquid glass is unconditional on every customer surface (claude/glass-only-remove-legacy-theme)

**Context.** The liquid-glass rollout reached 100% — the staged PRs (#2396–#2425) put glass markup on every customer page behind release gates. Owner directive this session: remove the old navy / warm-sand theme entirely and make glass the ONLY render on every customer-facing React surface, report, estimate, and email. Until now each surface still carried a pre-glass code path behind a server gate (`GATE_ESTIMATE_GLASS` / `GATE_REPORT_GLASS` / `GATE_PORTAL_GLASS` / `GATE_EMAIL_GLASS`) plus a per-render resolver (`glassReleaseActive` / `portalGlassInitial` / `watchPortalGlassDefault` / `glassParamRequested`) with `?glass=1` / `?glass=0` overrides — so the old theme was the fallback and one query-param away, and the "pro" financial pages (receipt / pay / statement) + the project report were still `?glass=1`-only dark launches, rendering the old theme by default in prod. Two owner calls: (1) FULL removal — delete the gates, the pre-glass branches, and the `?glass=0` escape hatch, leaving no rollback flag; (2) INCLUDE emails.

**Change.**
- **Gates retired** (`server/config/feature-gates.js`): the four `*GlassTheme` keys removed. Server payload/flag consumers collapsed to always-glass — `reports-public.js` + `public-lawn-diagnostic.js` send `glassDefault: true` for the live view; `public-ui-flags.js` always returns `{ portalGlass: true }` (kept as a compat shim so a stale Capacitor bundle that still polls it stays on glass); `estimate-public.js` keeps `glassCategoryEligible` (see estimate note) minus the theme gate. Unused `feature-gates` requires dropped from the report routes.
- **Client engine** (`client/src/glass/glass-engine.js`): removed `glassReleaseActive`, `glassParamRequested`, `portalGlassInitial`, and `watchPortalGlassDefault` (the `/api/public/ui-flags` fetch + localStorage cache + fail-closed revert). `useGlassSurface` / scene builder / `fireGlassConfetti` unchanged. Every customer surface now mounts the scene unconditionally: portal shell + login, `App` auth-check screen, booking (native + public), reschedule, prep guide, recap, contract sign, service outline, rate, lawn-care-included, newsletter landing/archive, track (+ preview), service + lawn reports, project report, and the pro financial pages (receipt / pay / statement) which always mount the quiet `'pro'` scene. Pre-glass ternaries (`glassActive ? glass : old`) collapsed to the glass branch across all pages; genuine non-glass conditions preserved (`mode === 'live'` on reports so pdf/static/sms_preview never mount the scene; `!isCertificate` on project reports).
- **Estimate — theme decoupled from copy** (owner call): the glass THEME is now unconditional on every estimate category (`EstimateViewPage` mounts `<EstimateGlassTheme active />`), but the new glass marketing COPY stays category-scoped (pest + lawn shipped; other categories pending copy-pack approval, per the 2026-07-05 directive). `glassCopyActive()` and the server's `glassCategoryEligible` → `glassDefault` flag are unchanged; they now gate COPY only. This lands visual glass everywhere without shipping unapproved copy, and keeps the change theme-only (no copy strings touched — "visual and content never share a PR").
- **Email — glass unconditional** (`server/services/email-template.js`, `email-template-library.js`): `wrapEmail` / `wrapServiceEmail` / `wrapNewsletter` return the glass renderers directly; `activeTheme()` always returns `GLASS_THEME`; `CLASSIC_THEME` and the pre-glass wrapper branches deleted; the library's `glassChrome` gate collapsed. (The email suite previously exercised classic output because `GATE_EMAIL_GLASS` was opt-in in every env; its assertions are theme-agnostic, so it stays green.)
- Removed the now-dead `useGlassProGate` (EstimateGlassTheme) plus unused imports/vars, and refreshed stale gate-referencing comments across the pages.

**Verification.** Client `vite build` clean. Vitest: glass-engine 9/9, estimate-glass-copy 19/19, estimate-glass-slots 9/9. Jest: `public-ui-flags` + `reports-public-glass-default` (both rewritten to the unconditional contract), `estimate-glass-category-scope` 31/31 (copy scope intact), and the full email suite — invoice / appointment / late-payment / project-prep / automation / hygiene, 94 tests — all green with glass now the only chrome. `check:portal-brand` clean (0 violations). No live DB in-session. Note: the `?glass=0` escape hatch is intentionally gone (owner call, full removal), so there is no in-app rollback flag — a glass regression would need a code revert.

## 2026-07-07 — Estimate View audit remediation: polish batch + SSR parity (rides the portal UI batch)

**Context.** The 2026-07-07 estimate-view audit (report: `~/Downloads/estimate-audit-2026-07-07/REPORT.md`) ranked eight findings beyond the `?glass=0` retirement (logged above). This batch lands the remaining code-level fixes in the rig working tree, to ship with the owner-approved portal UI batch. The audit's #4 — the server-rendered estimate (`server/routes/estimate-public.js`) diverging from the React page — was the named ship-blocker: 62–84px price vs React's 40px, 34 uses of the retired #6B7280 gray, a 1040px container vs 720px, no print CSS, and duplicate ad-hoc money formatters.

**Change.**
- **Safe-area (audit #2):** the React book bar offsets by `env(safe-area-inset-bottom/left/right)`; WavesShell's sticky header pads by `safe-area-inset-top`. (The SSR q-bar/toast/body already carried the bottom inset.)
- **Tabular digits (audit #8):** `fontVariantNumeric: 'tabular-nums'` at the 13 React money sites (line items, totals, discounts, annual ranges — EstimateViewPage, PriceCard, PaymentPreferenceButtons) and one consolidated CSS rule at the SSR equivalents (`.big-price .num/.anchor`, `.pt-price`, `.payment-summary-row strong`, `.supplemental-service-row strong`, `td.val`, `.wg-row-val`, `.manual-discount-row strong`, `.billing-total-row`).

The SSR page mirrors the same map (`stateHero` in `renderPage`); declined keeps the standard "Your estimate · {service}" kicker.
- **Token/format consolidation:** `components/estimate/tokens.js` is the one canonical `W` palette (13 copy-pasted palettes deleted; brand-red #C8102E vs estimate-red #C8312F and the two golds kept deliberately separate, documented in the file header; ReportShowcase's stray green → #15803D). `lib/money.js` gains `fmtMoneySigned()` — typographic minus (U+2212), no accounting parentheses — wired at the 3 React discount sites; the 3 SSR discount rows use the same U+2212. `PRICE_FONT = clamp(24px, 10.5vw, 40px)` is the single price size for the decision number.
- **Spacing/type sweeps:** ~157 off-scale spacing declarations migrated to the 4/8/12/16/20/24/32 scale (control/chip paddings and well/negative-margin cases exempted per the audit); off-scale type sizes normalized to the 11–40 scale incl. the ReportShowcaseCard fractional sizes and the lone 21px/weight-650.
- **SSR parity (audit #4):** price clamp unified to the React 40px token, #6B7280 → #475569 sweep (34 sites), container 1040→720px, `@media print` block (hide fixed chrome, white background, `break-inside: avoid` on cards — same contract as the React print fix), money rendering consolidated onto the route's `fmtMoney`.

**Verification.** Client: vitest estimate suites green, `vite build` clean (mechanical batch checkpoint: 81/81).
